The Meaning of Independent Efficient Cause
Al-Iji defines the independent efficient cause.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the precise definition of an independent efficient cause (علة مستقلة) in the context of infinite regress arguments.

Core Idea
An independent cause has no partner in the causal chain.

Al-Iji begins by clarifying what it means for a contingent to depend on an independent cause. He specifies that independence means having no partner in influencing the entire chain. This definition is crucial for the subsequent proof that infinite regress is impossible.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic definition
Read the Arabic passage that defines 'independent cause' and note the emphasis on 'no partner' (لا شريك).
2
Understand the condition
The passage explains that if a cause had a partner, it would not be independent. Understand why this matters for the regress argument.
3
Connect to the impossibility of regress
Reflect on how this definition sets up the proof that infinite regress is impossible, as we must require an external cause.
This will be continued in the next lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المرصد الخامس - المقصد الثامن : التسلسل محال أن يستند الممكن إلى علة مستقلة بالتأثير على معنى أن لا يكون له شريك في التأثير في تلك السلسلة، وإلا كان ذلك البعض مؤثراً في نفسه؛ لأنه ممكن، فلا بد له من علة مؤثرة، ولا يمكن أن تكون تلك العلة المؤثرة غير ذلك البعض، وإلا لم يكن ذلك البعض مستقلا بالتأثير في السلسلة، بل كان له شريك فيه ولا يمكن أن يكون في السلسلة المفروضة بعض مستغن عن المؤثر، كما في المركب من الواجب والممكن، وبهذا تبين بطلان ما قد قيل : من أنه يجوز أن يكون ما قبل المعلول الأخير علة للجميع، وهو معلول لما
The Fifth Observation - Eighth Proposition: Infinite regress is impossible for a contingent to depend on an independent efficient cause, meaning that it has no partner in influencing that chain. Otherwise, that part would be influencing itself, because it is contingent, so it must have an influencing cause, and that influencing cause cannot be other than that part, otherwise that part would not be independent in influencing the chain, but would have a partner in it. And it is impossible for there to be in the supposed chain a part that is independent of the influencer, as in the composite of the Necessary and the contingent. And by this the falsity of what has been said becomes clear: that it is permissible for what is before the last effect to be the cause of the whole, while it is itself an effect...
Source pages p. 172

Commentary
This passage elaborates on the definition of an independent efficient cause in the context of proving the impossibility of regress. It begins by restating the impossibility of a contingent depending on an independent cause, but now specifies that independence means having no partner in the causal influence on the chain. The argument then proceeds: if a part of the chain were independent, any other part that influenced it would make it a partner, or if the part influenced itself, that would be circular. The cause must be external to the chain. It then refutes a specific objection: that the penultimate effect (the one before the last effect) might be the cause of the whole chain. The refutation shows that this position would entail that the penultimate effect is both cause and effect in an unacceptable way, or that the chain would still require an external cause. The passage ends with 'وهو معلول لما', likely indicating the penultimate effect is itself an effect of something else, leading to regress or dependence on an external cause.

Key Terms
علة مستقلة
شريك

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think 'independent cause' means the cause has no external cause itself.
Correction: In this context, it specifically means the cause has no partner in causing the chain, not that it is uncaused.

Checkpoint
What does 'independent efficient cause' (علة مستقلة) mean in this passage?
A) It has no partner in influencing the chain
B) It is itself uncaused
C) It causes all parts of the chain directly
D) It is the last effect in the chain

Key Takeaway
An independent cause in this argument is defined as having no partner in the chain of causation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In your daily life, do you ever rely on created things or people as if they were independent causes, expecting them to determine your outcomes without needing Allah? What would it look like to truly depend on Allah alone as the ultimate independent cause?
?
This passage shows that no part of a causal chain can be independent. How does this challenge your sense of self-sufficiency? Are there areas where you secretly believe you are the 'independent cause' of your own success or goodness?
?
If an independent cause in creation is impossible, what does that mean for your relationship with Allah? Will you today examine your heart and repent of any subtle shirk in attributing independent power to anyone besides Him?

Refutation of the Penultimate Effect as Cause of the Whole
Al-Iji refutes the claim that the penultimate effect causes the whole.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the penultimate effect cannot be the cause of the entire chain and how this refutes a specific counterclaim.

Core Idea
The penultimate effect cannot be the cause of the whole because it itself is an effect.

After defining the independent cause, al-Iji refutes a specific objection: that the penultimate effect (the one before the last) could be the cause of the whole chain. He argues that this is impossible because that penultimate effect is itself an effect of something else, leading to a contradiction or infinite regress.

Guided Path
1
Read the refutation passage
Read the Arabic text that addresses the counterclaim about the penultimate effect.
2
Identify the counterclaim
Note the claim being refuted: that the cause before the last effect could be the cause of the whole.
3
Understand the refutation
The passage argues that this position leads to an impossible situation where the penultimate effect both causes and is caused, or requires an external cause, thus defeating the claim.
4
Connect to the overall proof
Understand how this refutation supports the main argument against infinite regress.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المرصد الخامس - المقصد الثامن : التسلسل محال أن يستند الممكن إلى علة مستقلة بالتأثير على معنى أن لا يكون له شريك في التأثير في تلك السلسلة، وإلا كان ذلك البعض مؤثراً في نفسه؛ لأنه ممكن، فلا بد له من علة مؤثرة، ولا يمكن أن تكون تلك العلة المؤثرة غير ذلك البعض، وإلا لم يكن ذلك البعض مستقلا بالتأثير في السلسلة، بل كان له شريك فيه ولا يمكن أن يكون في السلسلة المفروضة بعض مستغن عن المؤثر، كما في المركب من الواجب والممكن، وبهذا تبين بطلان ما قد قيل : من أنه يجوز أن يكون ما قبل المعلول الأخير علة للجميع، وهو معلول لما
The Fifth Observation - Eighth Proposition: Infinite regress is impossible for a contingent to depend on an independent efficient cause, meaning that it has no partner in influencing that chain. Otherwise, that part would be influencing itself, because it is contingent, so it must have an influencing cause, and that influencing cause cannot be other than that part, otherwise that part would not be independent in influencing the chain, but would have a partner in it. And it is impossible for there to be in the supposed chain a part that is independent of the influencer, as in the composite of the Necessary and the contingent. And by this the falsity of what has been said becomes clear: that it is permissible for what is before the last effect to be the cause of the whole, while it is itself an effect...

Commentary
This passage elaborates on the definition of an independent efficient cause in the context of proving the impossibility of regress. It begins by restating the impossibility of a contingent depending on an independent cause, but now specifies that independence means having no partner in the causal influence on the chain. The argument then proceeds: if a part of the chain were independent, any other part that influenced it would make it a partner, or if the part influenced itself, that would be circular. The cause must be external to the chain. It then refutes a specific objection: that the penultimate effect (the one before the last effect) might be the cause of the whole chain. The refutation shows that this position would entail that the penultimate effect is both cause and effect in an unacceptable way, or that the chain would still require an external cause. The passage ends with 'وهو معلول لما', likely indicating the penultimate effect is itself an effect of something else, leading to regress or dependence on an external cause.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that the penultimate effect (the one just before the final effect) could be the cause of the entire chain.
Correction: The passage shows that this is impossible because the penultimate effect is itself an effect of something else, so it cannot be the independent cause.

Checkpoint
What is the counterclaim refuted in this passage?
A) That the last effect causes the whole
B) That the penultimate effect causes the whole
C) That the chain has no cause
D) That the chain is infinite

Key Takeaway
The penultimate effect cannot be the cause of the entire chain because it is itself an effect.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In your own life, which created causes—people, possessions, achievements—do you tend to rely on as if they were independent? How can you consciously redirect your trust to the Only Independent Cause, Allah?
?
The penultimate effect cannot cause the whole. Are you treating any intermediate goal (like career, family, or even worship) as the ultimate cause of your happiness or success? What would change if you saw all these as dependent on Allah alone?
?
When you succeed, how often do you feel self-sufficient? Take a moment to recall a recent success. Can you sincerely acknowledge that every factor in that success was dependent on Allah? What specific step will you take today to express that dependence?

Objection and Response on the Meaning of Independent Cause
Objection and refutation on independence definition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the objection concerning the definition of an independent cause and how the commentator refutes it, reinforcing the first proof's validity.

Core Idea
The objection fails because the aggregate itself requires a cause, reverting to self-causation.

This passage addresses a subtle objection to the first proof's claim that a contingent needs an independent cause without any partner. The objector tries to show that partial independence is sufficient, but the commentator demonstrates that this leads to an infinite regress or self-causation, thus preserving the proof.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Notice how the objector distinguishes between internal and external partners.
The objection has two interpretations of 'no partner'.
2
Identify the two interpretations
Find where the objector says: if no partner at all (internal/external) vs. no external partner only. Understand the concessive argument.
The objector grants the second but denies the conclusion of self-causation.
3
Follow the refutation
The commentator shows that the objection reverts to a previous one about parts and wholes. Then he provides a counter-argument focusing on the penultimate cause's independence.
Pay attention to the role of the 'last effect' and the 'aggregate'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (على معنى أن لا يكون له شريك إلخ) قيل عليه : إن أراد أن لا يكون لها شريك أصلاً، لا خارج ولا داخل فلا نسلم احتياج الممكن إلى موجد كذلك . وإن أراد أن لا يكون لها شريك خارج ،فمسلم لكن لا نسلم لزوم كون ذلك البعض مؤثراً في نفسه؛ لجواز أن يكون ذلك البعض مجموع ما قبل المعلول علة مستقلة غير محتاج إلى خارج للجملة، ويكون علة ذلك المجموع ما قبله بواحد ، وهلم جرا. فلم يندفع بهذا التقرير الاعتراض الآتي، ولم يتبين فساده أقول : هذا رجوع إلى الاعتراض الثالث؛ لأن حاصله أن تعليل المجموع باعتبار تعليل كل جزء ه بآخر إلا أنه اعتبر الأجزاء هاهنا الجمل، وفيما سبق الآحاد وحينئذ يعود ما مر سابقاً أن من تلك الجمل مغاير لكل واحد من الجمل، فلا بد له من ،علة ولا يجوز أن يكون نفسه لامتناع تقدم الشيء على نفسه ولا جزءه؛ لأنه لا بد أن يكون علة لكل واحد من أجزائه، فيكون علة لنفسه، فتكون خارجة عنه ويلزم الانقطاع. منه مجموع لمجموع ( ج د ) مع استناد الأجزاء إلى الأجزاء، وما يقال : كل جزء يفرض علة للتسلسل، فعليته أولى منه بالعلية لها فيلزم ترجيح المرجوح مدفوع بأن ما قبل المعلول الأخير الذي ليس علة لشيء من آحاد السلسلة أولى بالعلية للسلسلة من سائر الأجزاء؛ لاستقلاله بإيجادها من غير احتياج إلى معاون بخلاف غيره من الأجزاء فإنه يحتاج إلى معاون في الإيجاد، وهو العلة القريبة. وأما المعلول الأخير فليس بمعاون في إيجاد السلسلة؛ إذ ليس علة لشيء أصلا. قوله : ( وبهذا تبين بطلان ما قد قيل قد عرفت بما حررناه في الحاشية السابقة اندفاع هذا الكلام . فإن قلت المراد بالعلة في تقرير الدليل هو الفاعل المستقل على معنى أن لا يستند شيءٍ من أجزاء السلسلة إلا إليه أو إلى ما صدر عنه، وما قبل المعلول الأخير لا إلى نهاية ليس فاعلاً مستقلاً بهذا المعنى، وهو ظاهر وأيضاً ما قبل المعلول الأخير لم يجب به جملة السلسلة، بل وجب به المعلول الأخير، ووجب بهما الجملة لا بالأول وحده والكلام فيما تجب الجملة به، فاندفع الاعتراض . قلت : الجواب عن الأول الذي ذكره المصنف في الإلهيات أن المعلوم لنا هو أن كل ممكن مركب من الممكنات لا بد له من فاعل مستقل، بمعنى أن لا يحتاج المركب إلى فاعل خارج عنه وفيما قيل المعلول الأخير استقلال بهذا المعنى، وأما الاحتياج إلى فاعل مستقل بذلك المعنى فلا نسلم ذلك، وعن الثاني الذي ذكره الشارح في حواشي التجريد أن المعلول الأخير مع مجموع ما قبله نفس جملة السلسلة، فكيف يتصور وجوب السلسلة بهما، وهو تعليل
His statement: (meaning that he has no partner, etc.). It was objected: If he intends that it has no partner at all, neither external nor internal, then we do not grant that the contingent needs an originator in that way. And if he intends that it has no external partner, then it is granted but we do not grant the necessity of that part being effective upon itself, because it is possible that that part is the aggregate of what is before the effect, an independent cause not needing an external for the whole, and the cause of that aggregate is what is before it by one, and so on. So this formulation does not repel the following objection, and its corruption is not shown. I say: This is a return to the third objection, because its gist is that the causation of the aggregate is by virtue of the causation of each part by another, except that here he considers the parts as wholes, and previously as individuals, and then what passed earlier returns: that each of those wholes is other than each of the individuals, so it must have a cause, and it cannot be itself because of the impossibility of a thing preceding itself, nor can it be its part, because it must be the cause of each of its parts, so it would be the cause of itself, thus it would be outside it and cut-off results. ... And it is said: every part that is assumed to be a cause of the series—its causality is prior to its being caused by it—so the preference of the inferior is required. This is repelled by the fact that what is before the last effect, which is not a cause of any individual of the series, is more entitled to causality of the series than the other parts, because of its independence in bringing it into existence without needing an assistant, unlike other parts which need an assistant in bringing into existence, which is the proximate cause. As for the last effect, it is not an assistant in bringing the series into existence, since it is not a cause of anything at all. His statement: (And by this the invalidity of what was said becomes clear.) ... Then if you say: The intended meaning of 'cause' in the formulation of the proof is the independent agent, meaning that no part of the series depends except on it or on what proceeds from it, and what is before the last effect ad infinitum is not an independent agent in this sense, and that is apparent. Also, the whole series is not necessitated by what is before the last effect; rather, the last effect is necessitated by it, and the whole is necessitated by both together, not by the first alone, and the discussion is concerning that by which the whole is necessitated, so the objection is repelled. I say: The answer to the first, which the author mentioned in Ilahiyyat, is that what is known to us is that every contingent composite of contingents must have an independent agent, meaning that the composite does not need an external agent, and in what was said, the last effect is independent in this sense. As for the need for an independent agent in that sense, we do not grant that. And the answer to the second, which the commentator mentioned in the glosses of al-Tajrid, is that the last effect together with the aggregate of what precedes it is the very whole of the series, so how can the necessitation of the series by both be imagined? That is the explanation.
Source pages p. 172

Commentary
This passage is a commentary responding to an objection about the meaning of 'independent cause' in the first proof. The objection raises two interpretations: if independence means no partner at all (internal or external), the opponent does not grant that the contingent needs such an originator; if it means no external partner, the opponent grants it but does not grant the conclusion of self-causation, because the part could be an aggregate that is independent with respect to the whole, while the aggregate depends on its parts which depend on earlier ones. The commentator shows that this reverts to a previous objection about parts and wholes, and then provides a detailed refutation. The response distinguishes between the cause of the individual parts and the cause of the aggregate, and argues that the penultimate cause is more entitled to causality of the series because it does not need an assistant. A further objection about the phrase 'and by this the invalidity becomes clear' is answered by clarifying that the independent cause means something on which no part depends except it, and that the last effect together with what precedes it constitutes the whole series, so the series cannot be necessitated by both.

علة مستقلة
مؤثراً في نفسه
مجموع ما قبل المعلول
العلة القريبة
الفاعل المستقل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the objection successfully refutes the proof by showing that partial independence (no external partner) is sufficient without requiring a fully independent cause.
Correction: The commentary shows that the objection fails because the aggregate itself requires a cause, leading back to self-causation or infinite regress.

Checkpoint
According to the commentary, what is the problem with the objection that the part could be an aggregate independent of external partners?
A) The aggregate itself would need a cause, leading to regress.
B) The aggregate is identical to the whole series.
C) The aggregate is not independent from internal parts.
D) The objection misunderstands the definition of 'cause'.

Key Takeaway
The objection fails because every aggregate requires a cause, which leads back to the original argument for an independent cause without any partner.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever rely on a collection of causes—your skills, resources, social connections, or luck—as if they are independent, forgetting that every part of that 'aggregate' is itself dependent on Allah? Where in your life have you acted as if the composite is self-sufficient without looking to the true independent Cause?
?
The objector tried to redefine independence to avoid acknowledging a single, external, all-powerful Cause. When have you rationalized or redefined your understanding of tawheed to make it more comfortable, avoiding the full implication that Allah alone is the independent cause of everything, including your own actions?
?
The refutation shows that every aggregate requires a cause outside itself. In your spiritual life, have you been content with the 'last effect'—a good deed, a memorized verse, a moment of devotion—while ignoring that the entire chain of your efforts points back to Allah's sole provision? Will you today look beyond the immediate effect and thank Allah for every step of the causes that led to it?

The Objection from Numbers and the Logical Reply
Al-Isfahani presents the objection and reply concerning infinite regress and numbers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the objection from infinite numerical series does not invalidate the proof of the impossibility of infinite regress, based on the distinction between real existents and imaginary entities.

Core Idea
The difference between real and imaginary is the key to refuting the numbers objection.

Al-Isfahani now addresses a classic objection to the proof of the impossibility of infinite regress: the case of numbers, which seem to form an infinite series. He shows that numbers are merely mental constructs, not real beings, and therefore do not force the same logical consequences as actual causal chains. This lesson walks through the objection and the sophisticated reply.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
Read the passage where the proof is challenged by the infinite series of numbers. Notice how the objector claims the same reasoning should apply to numbers, yet numbers are infinite.
The objector uses two sequences: doubling one and doubling a thousand.
2
Grasp the reply's core distinction
The reply argues that the proof concerns real existents (effects and causes), while numbers are purely imaginary. Understand why this distinction matters.
Real existents are 'encompassed by existence' (ضبطها وجود); numbers are not.
3
Examine the two options
The reply offers two ways to see why no impossibility follows for numbers: either the sequences cease with the imagination, or they do not cease but no real equality is required.
Both options avoid contradiction because numbers lack real existence.
4
Appreciate the precise wording
Note the phrase 'has been encompassed by existence' and why 'gathered in existence' would be narrower. This covers both simultaneous and sequential existence.

المرصد الخامس - المقصد الثامن : التسلسل محال أن يستند الممكن إلى علة أيضاً متوقفاً على بيان كون العلة مع المعلول فيستدل به على تناهي هذه الأمور كلها. (وقد نقض ) هذا الدليل ( بمراتب الأعداد لأن الدليل قائم فيها مع عدم تناهيها)، وذلك لأنا نفرض جملتين من الأعداد إحداهما تضعيف الواحد مراراً غير متناهية، والأخرى تضعيف الألف كذلك، ثم نطبق إحداهما على الأخرى بأن نضع الأول من الزائدة بإزاء الأول من الناقصة ونسرد الكلام إلى آخره، مع أن هاتين الجملتين غير متناهيتين بالضرورة. (والجواب ) عن هذا النقض ( أن المعلولات)، بل ما يستدل التطبيق على بطلان التسلسل فيه قد ضبطها وجود، فليس المذكور الذي هو المعلولات وأخواتها أمراً وهمياً محضاً، يكون انقطاعها في التطبيق بانقطاع الوهم وذهابها فيه باعتباره، بخلاف مراتب الأعداد فإنها وهمية محضة فلا يكون ذهابها في التطبيق إلا باعتبار الوهم، لكنه عاجز عن ملاحظة تلك الأمور الوهمية التي لا تتناهى فتنقطع تلك الأمور بانقطاع الوهم عن تطبيقها، فلا يلزم محذور. وتحقيقه أن الأعداد لكونها وهمية محضة ليس فيها جملتان في نفس الأمر تطبقان فنختار أنهما أي الجملتين المفروضتين في الأعداد تنقطعان في التطبيق بانقطاع الوهم عن التطبيق، لعجزه. وليس يلزم من انقطاعهما انقطاع ما لا يتناهى في نفس الأمر حتى يكون محالاً إذ ليست الجملتان في نفس الأمر، فلا يتصور أن يكون انقطاعهما في نفس الأمر. أو نختار أنهما لا تنقطعان ولا يلزم من ذلك تساويهما في نفس الأمر، لأن هذا التساوي فرع وجودهما في نفس الأمر بخلاف ما له وجود في نفس الأمر، فإنه يلزم فيه أحد أمرين إما انقطاعه في نفس الأمر فيكون ما لا يتناهى في الواقع متناهيا فيه أو عدمه أي عدم انقطاعه في نفس الأمر فيلزم تساوي الجملتين الزائدة والناقصة، وكلاهما محال، لما عرفت. وإنما قلنا قد ضبطها وجود، ولم نقل قد اجتمعت في الوجود ليتناول كل ما له وجود إما معاً سواء كان بينها ترتب، أو لم معاً يكن، وإما على سبيل التعاقب أي بلا اجتماع في الوجود، فإن ترتبهما أي
The fifth observation - the eighth intention: The infinite regress is impossible for the possible to depend on a cause, depending on clarifying that the cause is simultaneous with the effect, so it is used to infer the finitude of all these things. And this proof has been refuted by the ranks of numbers because the proof holds in them while they are infinite. That is because we assume two sequences of numbers, one of them doubling the one an infinite number of times, and the other doubling the thousand likewise, then we apply one to the other by placing the first of the increasing opposite the first of the decreasing and continue the discourse to its end, while these two sequences are necessarily infinite. And the answer to this refutation is that the effects, rather what the application proves the invalidity of infinite regress in has been encompassed by existence, so the mentioned thing which is the effects and their likes is not a purely imaginary matter, such that its cessation in the application is by the cessation of the imagination and its vanishing therein by its consideration, contrary to the ranks of numbers for they are purely imaginary, so their vanishing in the application is only by the consideration of the imagination, but it is incapable of observing those imaginary things which are infinite, so those things cease with the cessation of the imagination from applying them, so no absurdity follows. And its verification is that numbers, because they are purely imaginary, do not contain in themselves two sequences that are applied, so we choose that they, i.e., the two assumed sequences in numbers, cease in the application with the cessation of the imagination from the application, due to its incapacity. And it does not follow from their cessation the cessation of what is infinite in itself so as to be impossible, since the two sequences are not in themselves, so it is not conceivable that their cessation is in themselves. Or we choose that they do not cease and it does not follow from that their equality in themselves, because this equality is a branch of their existence in themselves, contrary to what has existence in itself, for there follows in it one of two things: either its cessation in itself, so that which is infinite in reality becomes finite therein, or its non-cessation, i.e., its non-cessation in itself, so there follows the equality of the two sequences, the increasing and the decreasing, and both are impossible, as you have known. And we only said 'has been encompassed by existence' and did not say 'have gathered in existence' to include everything that has existence, either simultaneously, whether there is order between them or not together, or sequentially, i.e., without coexistence in existence, for their order, i.e.
Source pages p. 175

Commentary
This passage presents a classical objection to the proof of the impossibility of infinite regress (التسلسل) using the method of application (التطبيق), followed by a detailed reply distinguishing real from imaginary entities. The author first restates the proof: infinite regress is impossible for contingent beings depending on a cause, because the cause must coexist with the effect, leading to the finitude of all such chains. The objection is then raised: the same proof seems to apply to the ranks of numbers (مراتب الأعداد), where we can assume two infinite sequences (e.g., doubling one and doubling a thousand) and apply them to each other, yet numbers are obviously infinite. The reply begins by asserting that the entities in question in the proof (the effects and their causes) have been encompassed by existence (ضبطها وجود), meaning they are real beings that actually exist. In contrast, numbers are purely imaginary (وهمية محضة); they have no real existence in the external world. Therefore, when we imagine applying two infinite sequences of numbers, the application only occurs in the imagination, and when the imagination ceases, the sequences cease without any real consequence. The author then offers two choices to demonstrate why no impossibility follows: either the sequences cease with the cessation of the imagination (since they are imaginary), or they do not cease but no real equality between them is required because equality presupposes real existence. For real existents, if they were infinite, the application would force either the cessation of the infinite (making it finite) or the equality of two sequences that are not actually equal—both impossible. Finally, the author clarifies that the phrase 'has been encompassed by existence' is deliberately chosen to cover both simultaneous and sequential existence, ensuring that all real things, whether ordered or not, are included.

التسلسل
التطبيق
المعلولات
مراتب الأعداد
وهمي محض
ضبطها وجود
العلة مع المعلول

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the objection from infinite numerical series genuinely refutes the proof of the impossibility of infinite regress.
Correction: The reply shows that numbers are purely imaginary and do not have real existence, so the proof's reasoning does not apply to them. The proof remains valid for real causal chains.

Checkpoint
According to the reply, why does the objection from numbers not refute the proof of the impossibility of infinite regress?
A) Because numbers are infinite in actuality, making the proof invalid.
B) Because numbers are purely imaginary and lack real existence, so the application has no real effect.
C) Because the application method does not work for numbers due to their nature.
D) Because numbers are finite in reality.

Key Takeaway
The objection from numbers fails because numbers are imaginary, not real existents, so the proof against infinite regress remains valid for real beings.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you fear an outcome or cling to an excuse, is it based on a real existent or an imaginary construct? Will you examine it now and let go of what is purely imaginary?
?
The scholars refuted a seemingly logical objection by distinguishing real from imaginary. What objection do you nurse against Allah's commands that seems logical but is actually based on an imaginary assumption? Will you discard it today?
?
If the proof of Allah's existence stands firm like the impossibility of infinite regress, what chain of 'causes' do you still rely on instead of directly depending on the First Cause? How will you break that chain today?

Why the Argument from Application Does Not Apply to Numbers
The author refutes the objection from numbers by stating that numbers are purely imaginary.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the argument from application (tatbiq) against infinite regress does not apply to purely imaginary series like the ranks of numbers.

Core Idea
The argument from application only works for actual existents, not imaginary ones.

One common objection to the argument from application is that it would also prove the finitude of numbers, which are infinite. In this passage, the author refutes this by showing that numbers are purely imaginary and have no actual existence, so the argument does not apply to them.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice how the author distinguishes numbers from actual existents.
2
Identify the two choices
The author presents two alternative ways to handle the number objection: either the two series are interrupted by imagination, or they are not interrupted but no equality follows. Find these two choices.
3
Understand the key distinction
Understand why the objection fails: numbers are purely imaginary, so their 'interruption' does not entail finitude in actual reality.
The argument only applies to things that exist in actual reality.

المذكور بمنع جريان الدليل في الأعداد كما فصل في الشرح. ونحن نجيب عنه بمنع تخلف الحكم في صورة النقض إذ الحكم هاهنا استحالة وجود أمور غير متناهية والحكم في مراتب الأعداد كذلك لأنها وإن كانت غير متناهية أصلاً وليس في الوجود الذهني أيضاً لاستحالة وجودها قوله : ( فإن ترتب هذين إلخ) في بعض النسخ بصيغة التفعيل والمراد منه التطبيق، وفي بعضها بصيغة التفعل والمراد منه الحصول إذ ليس الترتيب والترتب بمعنى وليس مرتبة جزءاً مما فوقها كما مر . قوله : (وتلخيص ما ذكروه من كون امتناع التسلسل مشروطاً بشرطين. وتلخيص التلخيص : أن التطبيق التفصيلي ممتنع في الأمور الغير المتناهية مطلقاً فلا يجري البرهان في شيء من الصور فالمراد التطبيق الإجمالي وهو إنما يجري في الأمور المجتمعة المترتبة دون غيرها كما لخصه . قوله : ( إذ ليست مجتمعة بحسب الخارج إلخ) والوقوع المذكور إذا كان عارضاً في الخارج يقتضي وجود الطرفين في الخارج معا والجواب أن الاتصاف بالوقوع المذكور إذا كان حقيقياً فالحال كما لو ذكرت وأما إذا كان انتزاعياً فلا يقتضي إلا وجود الموصوف في الخارج بحيث إذا لاحظ العقل انتزع منه الصفة والوقوع المذكور كذلك كالتعاقب فلا حاجة إلى الاجتماع وهو يكفي لنا في الاستدلال فإن كون السلسلة الغير متناهية في الخارج بحالة إذا لاحظها العقل قوله: (ليسقط عنهم ذلك النقض وجه سقوط النقض بمراتب الأعداد عندهم ليس عدمية العدد فإنه موجود عندهم، بل عدم الترتب بناء على ما هو المختار عندهم من أن كل عدد مركب من الوحدات لا الأعداد التي تحته كما سيأتي، وبهذا يظهر أن النقض على من الحكماء بجزئية بعض الأعداد من البعض، وعدم تناهي The Fifth Observatory - The Eighth Objective: The regress is impossible. The contingent cannot be dependent on a cause until the application (tatbiq) used to prove the invalidity of the regress has [its] existence fixed. So the mentioned [series], which is the effects and their likes, is not a purely imaginary thing, such that its interruption in the application is due to the interruption of imagination and its disappearance in it by virtue of it, unlike the ranks of numbers, for they are purely imaginary, so their disappearance in the application is only by virtue of imagination, but it is incapable of observing those imaginary things that are infinite, so those things are interrupted by the interruption of imagination from applying them, so no absurdity follows. And its verification: numbers, being purely imaginary, do not have two series in actual reality that are applied, so we choose that they, i.e., the two supposed series in numbers, are interrupted in the application by the interruption of imagination from application, due to its incapacity. And it does not follow from their interruption the interruption of what is infinite in actual reality such that it would be impossible, since the two series are not in actual reality, so it cannot be conceived that their interruption is in actual reality. Or we choose that they are not interrupted, and it does not follow from that their equality in actual reality, because this equality is a branch of their existence in actual reality, unlike what has existence in actual reality, for then one of two things necessarily follows: either its interruption in actual reality, so that what is infinite in reality becomes finite in it, or its non-interruption in actual reality, so that the equality of the two series, the excessive and the deficient, follows, and both are impossible, as you have known. And we only said 'its existence is fixed' and did not say 'they have gathered in existence' to encompass everything that has existence, either together, whether there is order between them or not together, or sequentially, i.e., without coexistence in existence, for the ordering of these two types... His saying: 'We choose that they are interrupted' means on the supposition of imagining them and applying them in detail. His saying: 'And we choose that they are not interrupted' means on the supposition of imagining them and applying them in summary, and it is possible that the word 'or' is for choice, i.e., we have the choice of each of the two alternatives and the ordered impossibility does not follow. All of them answered the mentioned objection by denying the application of the proof to numbers as detailed in the commentary. And we answer it by denying the failure of the ruling in the case of the objection, for the ruling here is the impossibility of the existence of infinite things, and the ruling regarding the ranks of numbers is likewise, because although they are infinite, their existence is not possible for us, for number according to the theologians (mutakallimun) is among the relational things, so its existence cannot occur externally at all, and in the mind it is infinite in detail and there is no regress in its existence in the mind likewise in summary. This is his statement, and I say: Among the objection is that the completion of the proof entails an impossibility, as the commentator (sharh) clarified in the glosses of al-Matali', and the mentioned objection is of this kind, for its summary is that if the proof were sound, it would indicate the finitude of the ranks of numbers even if they are relational, because the proof runs in them while they are infinite in actual reality, so the answer then is what the investigators (muhaqqiqun) mentioned, not what he mentioned here from the aspects of the master (ustadh), so let it be considered. The Fifth Observatory - The Eighth Objective: The regress is impossible. The contingent cannot be dependent on a cause [with] the ordering of these two types, namely, those gathered in existence and those sequential in it, and not merely by consideration of imagination, as in the ranks of numbers, because the units in them have been characterized by existence in actual reality, either gathered or sequential. And the philosophers (hukama') said: Regress is only impossible in things that have actual existence and order, either positional or natural, to remove from them that objection. And a summary of what they mentioned: that if the units exist together actually and there is order between them as well, then if the first of one series is placed opposite the first of the other series, the second is opposite the second definitely, and so on, so the application is completed without doubt. And if they do not exist together externally, it is not completed, because the occurrence of the units of one opposite the units of the other is not in external existence, since they are not gathered externally at any time, nor in mental existence either, due to the impossibility of their existence. His saying: 'For the ordering of these two, etc.' In some copies it is in the active form (taf'il) and what is meant is application, and in some it is in the reflexive form (tafa''ul) and what is meant is occurrence, since order and ranking are not in the sense of placing some units before others or their precedence considered according to the theologian. His saying: 'To remove, etc.' The necessary for the purpose, i.e., so that objection is removed either due to the lack of actual existence of numbers as is the verification, or due to the lack of order, because all their ranks are composed of units and no rank is a part of what is above it as has passed. His saying: 'And a summary of what they mentioned from the fact that the impossibility of regress is conditioned by two conditions. And a summary of the summary: that detailed application is impossible in infinite things absolutely, so the proof does not run in any of the forms, so what is meant is the summary application, which only runs in things that are gathered and ordered, unlike others, as he summarized it. His saying: 'Since they are not gathered externally, etc.' And the mentioned occurrence, if it is an accident in the external, necessitates the existence of both ends externally together, and the answer is that the characterization by the mentioned occurrence, if it is real, the situation is as you mentioned, but if it is abstractive, it only necessitates the existence of the described in the external such that if the intellect observes it, it abstracts the attribute from it, and the mentioned occurrence is like that, like succession, so there is no need for gathering, and it suffices for us in the inference, for the fact that the infinite chain is in the external in a state such that if the intellect observes it... His saying: 'The removal from them of that objection' The aspect of the removal of the objection by the ranks of numbers for them is not the non-existence of number, for it exists for them, but rather the lack of order, based on what is chosen for them that every number is composed of units, not the numbers under it, as will come, and by this it appears that the objection against those philosophers who hold the partiality of some numbers to others, and the infinity of rational souls for example, is certainly valid, unless they assert the non-existence of the unit, so understand. His saying: 'Since they are not gathered externally at any time' There is discussion in it, because events...
Source pages p. 176

Commentary
This passage is a detailed refutation of an objection to the argument from application (tatbiq) against infinite regress (tasalsul), followed by an exposition of the proper conditions for the argument. The author first addresses the objection that the argument would apply to the ranks of numbers, which are infinite but purely imaginary. He explains that the argument only applies to things that have actual existence; numbers are purely imaginary (wahmiyya mahda), so their interruption in the application is merely due to the limitation of imagination, not because they actually become finite. He then offers two choices regarding the supposed series in numbers: either they are interrupted by imagination, or they are not interrupted but no equality follows since they have no actual existence. For actual existents, however, one of two impossibilities follows: either the series becomes finite, or the two series (excessive and deficient) become equal, both impossible. The author then clarifies why he used the phrase 'its existence is fixed' (qad dabataha wujud) instead of 'they have gathered in existence' (ijtama'at fi al-wujud): to cover both simultaneous and sequential existents. He then presents the philosophers' (hukama') refinement: the argument only applies to things with actual existence and order (either positional or natural). A summary of their view is given: if units exist together actually and are ordered, the application works; if not, it fails. The passage ends with several glosses (aqwal) explaining terms and further addressing the number objection, including a discussion of whether numbers are real and the implications for the argument.

Key Terms
تسلسل

وجود

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The argument from application would prove that numbers are finite, which is false, so the argument is invalid.
Correction: The argument only applies to actual existents, not imaginary ones. Numbers are imaginary, so the argument does not apply, and no contradiction arises.

Checkpoint
Why does the argument from application not apply to the ranks of numbers?
A) Because numbers are infinite and thus the argument fails.
B) Because numbers are purely imaginary and do not exist in actual reality.
C) Because the ranks of numbers are not ordered.
D) Because the argument only applies to non-causal series.

Key Takeaway
The argument from application only refutes infinite regress in actual existents; it does not apply to purely imaginary series like numbers.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think about the infinite nature of numbers, do you treat them as real things in your mind? This passage teaches that they are purely imaginary. How often do you mistake your own mental constructs for objective reality, especially when reasoning about Allah's existence and attributes? Will you commit to distinguishing between what exists in your imagination and what truly exists from today?
?
The author says the imagination is 'incapable of observing infinite imaginary things'. Have you ever rejected a theological truth (like the impossibility of an infinite regress) because you could not fully imagine it? What specific step will you take to trust sound reasoning and revelation over your limited imagination?
?
This lesson guards against the error of applying an argument to imaginary things as if they were real. In your own life, which intellectual or spiritual arguments have you dismissed because you applied them to the wrong kind of 'thing' (e.g., applying arguments meant for actual beings to thoughts or feelings)? How will you correct this habit to avoid missing the truth?

Causality and Created Things
intermediate
6 min
Conditions for the Argument from Application: Existence and Order
The author states the conditions for the application argument and presents the philosophers' refinement.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the conditions under which the argument from application is valid, namely that it applies only to things that actually exist and are ordered in some way.

Core Idea
The argument from application requires actual existence and real order.

After refuting the number objection, the author clarifies that the argument is only valid for things that have actual existence, whether simultaneously or sequentially. The philosophers further specify that regress is only impossible in things with actual existence and order, thereby avoiding the number objection altogether.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on conditions
Read the Arabic passage and translation. Notice the distinction between simultaneous and sequential existents.
2
Understand the two types of existents
The author explains that the argument applies to things that exist either together (simultaneously) or in succession (sequentially).
The phrase 'qad dabataha wujud' is used to cover both.
3
Learn the philosophers' two conditions
The philosophers (hukama') add that regress is impossible only in things with actual existence and order (either positional or natural).
This is why numbers are excluded: they lack actual existence and often order.

And a summary of the summary: that detailed application is impossible in infinite things absolutely, so the proof does not run in any of the forms, so what is meant is the summary application, which only runs in things that are gathered and ordered, unlike others, as he summarized it. His saying: 'Since they are not gathered externally, etc.' And the mentioned occurrence, if it is an accident in the external, necessitates the existence of both ends externally together, and the answer is that the characterization by the mentioned occurrence, if it is real, the situation is as you mentioned, but if it is abstractive, it only necessitates the existence of the described in the external such that if the intellect observes it, it abstracts the attribute from it, and the mentioned occurrence is like that, like succession, so there is no need for gathering, and it suffices for us in the inference, for the fact that the infinite chain is in the external in a state such that if the intellect observes it... His saying: 'The removal from them of that objection' The aspect of the removal of the objection by the ranks of numbers for them is not the non-existence of number, for it exists for them, but rather the lack of order, based on what is chosen for them that every number is composed of units, not the numbers under it, as will come, and by this it appears that the objection against those philosophers who hold the partiality of some numbers to others, and the infinity of rational souls for example, is certainly valid, unless they assert the non-existence of the unit, so understand. His saying: 'Since they are not gathered externally at any time' There is discussion in it, because events...
Source pages p. 176

Commentary
This passage is a detailed refutation of an objection to the argument from application (tatbiq) against infinite regress (tasalsul), followed by an exposition of the proper conditions for the argument. The author first addresses the objection that the argument would apply to the ranks of numbers, which are infinite but purely imaginary. He explains that the argument only applies to things that have actual existence; numbers are purely imaginary (wahmiyya mahda), so their interruption in the application is merely due to the limitation of imagination, not because they actually become finite. He then offers two choices regarding the supposed series in numbers: either they are interrupted by imagination, or they are not interrupted but no equality follows since they have no actual existence. For actual existents, however, one of two impossibilities follows: either the series becomes finite, or the two series (excessive and deficient) become equal, both impossible. The author then clarifies why he used the phrase 'its existence is fixed' (qad dabataha wujud) instead of 'they have gathered in existence' (ijtama'at fi al-wujud): to cover both simultaneous and sequential existents. He then presents the philosophers' (hukama') refinement: the argument only applies to things with actual existence and order (either positional or natural). A summary of their view is given: if units exist together actually and are ordered, the application works; if not, it fails. The passage ends with several glosses (aqwal) explaining terms and further addressing the number objection, including a discussion of whether numbers are real and the implications for the argument.

وجود
مجتمعة
متعاقبة
حكماء

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The argument from application applies to any infinite series, including numbers, so it is inconsistent.
Correction: The argument only applies to series with actual existence and real order. Numbers lack either existence or order, so they are not counterexamples.

The argument from application is valid only for series that have actual existence and real order; numbers and other imaginary series are excluded.

The Two Types of Series and the Condition for Impossibility
Al-Isfahani defines simultaneous and successive series and states the condition for impossibility of regress.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the distinction between simultaneous and successive series and the condition that regress is only impossible when the series has actual existence and order.

Core Idea
Regress is impossible only when the series actually exists and has an order.

Al-Isfahani begins by defining the two types of series relevant to the proof of the impossibility of infinite regress. He then states the condition set by the philosophers: regress is impossible only for series that have actual existence and a real order, whether positional or natural. This condition is crucial to refute the objection based on numbers.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Notice how Al-Isfahani introduces the two types and the condition.
2
Identify the two types of series
Find where Al-Isfahani mentions 'the simultaneous in existence' and 'the successive in existence'. Understand the difference between them.
Simultaneous series exist together at once; successive follow each other in time.
3
Understand the condition for impossibility
Notice the philosophers' condition: regress is impossible only in things that have actual existence (wujud bi al-fi'l) and order (tartib), either positional or natural.
This excludes merely mental or potential series.
4
Reflect on the number example
Consider why the series of numbers does not constitute a counterexample: although numbers have an order, they do not have actual existence as a series in the external world.
The units in numbers exist in reality either simultaneously or successively, but the series as a whole is not an actual existing thing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المرصد الخامس - المقصد الثامن : التسلسل محال أن يستند الممكن إلى علة ترتب هذين النوعين أعني المجتمعة في الوجود والمتعاقبة فيه ( وليس بمجرد اعتبار الوهم)، كما في مراتب الأعداد لأن الآحاد فيهما قد اتصفت بالوجود في نفس الأمر، إما مجتمعة وإما متعاقبة ) وقال الحكماء : إنما يمتنع التسلسل في أمور لها وجود بالفعل، وترتب إما وضعاً، وإما طبعاً ليسقط عنهم ذلك النقض ) . وتلخيص ما ذكروه : أنه إذا كانت الآحاد موجودة معاً بالفعل، وكان بينها ترتب أيضاً، فإذا جعل الأول من إحدى الجملتين بإزاء الأول من الجملة الأخرى كان الثاني بإزاء الثاني قطعاً، وهكذا. فيتم التطبيق بلا شبهة، وإذا لم تكن موجودة في الخارج معاً لم يتم لأن وقوع آحاد إحداهما بإزاء آحاد الأخرى ليس في الوجود الخارجي، إذ ليست مجتمعة بحسب الخارج في زمان أصلاً وليس في الوجود الذهني أيضاً لاستحالة وجودها
The Fifth Observatory - The Eighth Objective: Regress is impossible. That the contingent is dependent on a cause [requires] ordering these two types: the simultaneous in existence and the successive in it (and not merely by consideration of estimation), as in the ranks of numbers because the units in them are qualified by existence in reality, either simultaneous or successive. And the philosophers said: Regress is only impossible in things that have actual existence and order, either positional or natural, to refute that objection against them. And a summary of what they mentioned: If the units exist together actually and there is also order between them, then if the first of one series is placed opposite the first of the other series, the second is opposite the second necessarily, and so on. Thus the correspondence is completed without doubt. But if they do not exist together in the external world, it is not completed because the occurrence of units of one series opposite units of the other is not in external existence, since they are not together externally in any time at all, nor in mental existence either due to the impossibility of their existence.
Source pages p. 177

Commentary
This passage defines the two types of series relevant to the proof of the impossibility of infinite regress (al-tasalsul) and states the condition under which the proof of correspondence (burhan al-tatbiq) works. Al-Isfahani begins by stating that regress is impossible when the contingent depends on a cause that involves ordering of two types: (1) the simultaneous series (al-mujtami'a fi al-wujud) where all members exist together, and (2) the successive series (al-muta'aqiba fihi) where members follow each other in time. He clarifies that this ordering is not merely a mental consideration (wahm), as in the ranks of numbers where units are qualified by existence in reality either simultaneously or successively. Then he reports the philosophers' condition: regress is impossible only in things that have actual existence (wujud bi al-fi'l) and order (tartib), either positional (wad'an) or natural (tab'an). This condition is meant to refute the objection that numbers form an infinite series but do not lead to impossibility. The summary of their argument follows: if the units exist together actually and are ordered, then placing the first of one series opposite the first of the other forces the second opposite the second, and so on, yielding a perfect one-to-one correspondence. If they do not exist together externally, the correspondence fails because the pairing is not in external existence, nor even in mental existence since they cannot exist mentally together.

Key Terms

المجتمعة في الوجود
المتعاقبة
الوجود بالفعل
الترتب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the proof of correspondence requires both series to be actually infinite.
Correction: The condition here is about existence and order, not infinity per se. The series must have actual existence and real order for the impossibility to apply.

Checkpoint
What are the two types of series mentioned by Al-Isfahani in this passage?
A) Finite and infinite series
B) Simultaneous and successive series
C) Mental and external series
D) Causal and non-causal series

Key Takeaway
Impossibility of regress requires a series with actual existence and real order.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Will you break that chain today by grounding yourself in what truly exists—your present actions and relationship with Allah?
?

The Correspondence Proof and Its Requirements
Al-Isfahani explains the correspondence proof and its dependence on actual coexistence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the correspondence proof demonstrates the impossibility of regress and why it requires the series to exist together actually.

Core Idea
The correspondence proof works only when the series coexist in actual existence.

After establishing the condition, Al-Isfahani summarizes the philosophers' argument using the correspondence proof. He explains that if the units of two ordered series exist together actually, placing them in one-to-one correspondence leads to a contradiction. If they do not coexist, the proof fails because the correspondence cannot be established in external reality or even in the mind.

Guided Path
1
Read the summary of the proof
Read the Arabic passage beginning with 'وتلخيص ما ذكروه' and its translation. Understand the logical steps.
2
Understand the condition for successful correspondence
Notice that the proof requires two things: the units exist together actually (معاً بالفعل) and there is order between them.
If these hold, then placing first opposite first forces second opposite second, etc.
3
See why lack of coexistence breaks the proof
Al-Isfahani explains that if the units are not together externally, the pairing cannot be done in external existence, nor even in mental existence because they cannot all exist in the mind at once.
This is why numbers do not constitute a counterexample.
4
Reflect on the overall argument
Consider how this condition refutes the objection from the infinite series of numbers. Numbers have order but not actual coexistence as a series.

Source Text

Meaning of Tartib and the Purpose of the Refutation
Al-Isfahani explains the meaning of 'tartib' and the purpose of the refutation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the linguistic variants of 'tartib' and 'tatbiq' in the proof of correspondence, and the reason why the objection is refuted.

Core Idea
Order does not mean simple precedence; it means correspondence in causal arrangement.

Al-Isfahani begins by clarifying the terminology used in the earlier text. The phrase 'ordering of these two types' has been read in two ways, each pointing to a different nuance. He also explains the purpose of the refutation: either because infinite numbers are not actual or because their arrangement lacks true order.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the first part of the passage where Al-Isfahani comments on 'fa-in tarattub hadhayn' and 'li-yasqut'. Pay attention to the variant readings.
The variant readings alter the meaning slightly.
2
Identify the two variant readings
Notice that in some copies the word is in the causative form (taf`il) meaning correspondence, and in others in the reflexive form (tafa``ul) meaning occurrence. Understand why the author says 'order' does not mean simple precedence.
3
Understand the purpose of the refutation
Al-Isfahani explains that the objection falls away either because infinite numbers are not actual existents (as per the verified truth) or because they lack true order, since ranks are composed of units and no rank is part of another.
This is a key clarification for the validity of the proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( فإن ترتب هذين إلخ) في بعض النسخ بصيغة التفعيل والمراد منه التطبيق، وفي بعضها بصيغة التفعل والمراد منه الحصول إذ ليس الترتيب والترتب بمعنى تقديم بعض الأحاد على بعض أو تقدمه معتبراً عند المتكلم . قوله : (ليسقط إلخ) اللازم للغاية أي فيسقط ذلك النقض إما لعدم وجود الأعداد بالفعل كما هو التحقيق أو لعدم الترتب لأن جميع مراتبها مركبة من الوحدات وليس مرتبة جزءاً مما فوقها كما مر . قوله: (وتلخيص ما ذكروه من كون امتناع التسلسل مشروطاً بشرطين. وتلخيص التلخيص : أن التطبيق التفصيلي ممتنع في الأمور الغير المتناهية مطلقاً فلا يجري البرهان في شيء من الصور فالمراد التطبيق الإجمالي وهو إنما يجري في الأمور المجتمعة المترتبة دون غيرها كما لخصه .
His statement: '(For the ordering of these two, etc.)' – in some copies it is in the form of taf`il (causative) and the intended meaning is correspondence (tatbiq), and in some copies in the form of tafa``ul (reflexive) and the intended meaning is occurrence, since order (tartib) and orderedness (tarattub) do not mean the precedence of some units over others or their being prior as considered by the theologian. His statement: '(to refute, etc.)' – the necessary for the purpose, i.e., that refutation falls away either due to the non-existence of numbers actually as is the verification, or due to lack of order because all their ranks are composed of units and no rank is part of what is above it, as passed. His statement: '(And a summary of what they mentioned)' – that the impossibility of regress is conditional on two conditions. And a summary of the summary: that detailed correspondence (tatbiq tafseeli) is impossible in infinite things absolutely, so the proof does not apply in any form. So what is intended is general correspondence (tatbiq ijmali), and it only applies in things that are together and ordered, not others, as he summarized.
Source pages p. 177

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on three phrases from the previous text. Al-Isfahani first explains the phrase 'for the ordering of these two types' (fa-in tarattub hadhayn). He notes variant readings: in some copies the word is in the causative form (taf`il) meaning 'correspondence' (tatbiq), and in others in the reflexive form (tafa``ul) meaning 'occurrence' (husul). He clarifies that 'order' (tartib) and 'orderedness' (tarattub) do not mean the precedence of some units over others as the theologian considers. Second, he explains the phrase 'to refute' (li-yasqut) as indicating the purpose: the refutation of the objection falls away either because numbers are not actual existents (as is the verified truth) or because they lack order, since ranks are composed of units and no rank is part of the one above it. Third, he comments on the summary, noting that the impossibility of regress has two conditions. He then gives a summary of the summary: detailed correspondence (tatbiq tafseeli) is impossible in infinite things absolutely, so the proof (burhan) does not apply in any form. What is meant is general correspondence (tatbiq ijmali), which applies only to things that are together (mujtami'a) and ordered (mutarattiba), not to others. This explains the precise scope of the proof of correspondence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The term 'tartib' in this context means simple temporal or spatial precedence.
Correction: Al-Isfahani clarifies that 'tartib' does not mean precedence of some units over others; it means correspondence or causal arrangement.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
The term 'tartib' in the proof of correspondence denotes a causal relationship, not mere priority, and the objection to the proof fails because infinite series are either non-actual or non-ordered.

Two Types of Correspondence in the Proof of Regress
Al-Isfahani summarizes the two types of correspondence and their applicability.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the difference between detailed and general correspondence and why only general correspondence applies to infinite ordered things.

Core Idea
Detailed correspondence fails for infinities; only general correspondence works for simultaneous ordered series.

In this passage, Al-Isfahani summarizes the two conditions for the impossibility of regress and distinguishes between detailed and general correspondence. The proof of correspondence (burhan al-tatbiq) only functions when applied to things that are both together and ordered.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the second part of the passage where Al-Isfahani gives the summary. Focus on the two types of correspondence and their conditions.
2
Identify the two types of correspondence
Find the terms 'tatbiq tafseeli' (detailed correspondence) and 'tatbiq ijmali' (general correspondence). Understand that detailed is impossible for infinite things, while general is possible.
Detailed correspondence would require matching each unit individually, which is impossible.
3
Understand the conditions for the proof
Al-Isfahani states that general correspondence only applies to things that are together (mujtami'a) and ordered (mutarattiba). These are the two conditions. Grasp why both are necessary for the proof to work.
The two conditions correspond to the impossibility of regress being conditional on two conditions mentioned earlier.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( فإن ترتب هذين إلخ) في بعض النسخ بصيغة التفعيل والمراد منه التطبيق، وفي بعضها بصيغة التفعل والمراد منه الحصول إذ ليس الترتيب والترتب بمعنى تقديم بعض الأحاد على بعض أو تقدمه معتبراً عند المتكلم . قوله : (ليسقط إلخ) اللازم للغاية أي فيسقط ذلك النقض إما لعدم وجود الأعداد بالفعل كما هو التحقيق أو لعدم الترتب لأن جميع مراتبها مركبة من الوحدات وليس مرتبة جزءاً مما فوقها كما مر . قوله: (وتلخيص ما ذكروه من كون امتناع التسلسل مشروطاً بشرطين. وتلخيص التلخيص : أن التطبيق التفصيلي ممتنع في الأمور الغير المتناهية مطلقاً فلا يجري البرهان في شيء من الصور فالمراد التطبيق الإجمالي وهو إنما يجري في الأمور المجتمعة المترتبة دون غيرها كما لخصه .
His statement: '(For the ordering of these two, etc.)' – in some copies it is in the form of taf`il (causative) and the intended meaning is correspondence (tatbiq), and in some copies in the form of tafa``ul (reflexive) and the intended meaning is occurrence, since order (tartib) and orderedness (tarattub) do not mean the precedence of some units over others or their being prior as considered by the theologian. His statement: '(to refute, etc.)' – the necessary for the purpose, i.e., that refutation falls away either due to the non-existence of numbers actually as is the verification, or due to lack of order because all their ranks are composed of units and no rank is part of what is above it, as passed. His statement: '(And a summary of what they mentioned)' – that the impossibility of regress is conditional on two conditions. And a summary of the summary: that detailed correspondence (tatbiq tafseeli) is impossible in infinite things absolutely, so the proof does not apply in any form. So what is intended is general correspondence (tatbiq ijmali), and it only applies in things that are together and ordered, not others, as he summarized.
Source pages p. 177

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on three phrases from the previous text. Al-Isfahani first explains the phrase 'for the ordering of these two types' (fa-in tarattub hadhayn). He notes variant readings: in some copies the word is in the causative form (taf`il) meaning 'correspondence' (tatbiq), and in others in the reflexive form (tafa``ul) meaning 'occurrence' (husul). He clarifies that 'order' (tartib) and 'orderedness' (tarattub) do not mean the precedence of some units over others as the theologian considers. Second, he explains the phrase 'to refute' (li-yasqut) as indicating the purpose: the refutation of the objection falls away either because numbers are not actual existents (as is the verified truth) or because they lack order, since ranks are composed of units and no rank is part of the one above it. Third, he comments on the summary, noting that the impossibility of regress has two conditions. He then gives a summary of the summary: detailed correspondence (tatbiq tafseeli) is impossible in infinite things absolutely, so the proof (burhan) does not apply in any form. What is meant is general correspondence (tatbiq ijmali), which applies only to things that are together (mujtami'a) and ordered (mutarattiba), not to others. This explains the precise scope of the proof of correspondence.

Key Terms
التطبيق التفصيلي
التطبيق الإجمالي
شرطان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The proof of correspondence works for any infinite series, regardless of order or simultaneity.
Correction: Al-Isfahani specifies that detailed correspondence is impossible for infinites, and general correspondence only works for simultaneous and ordered series.

Checkpoint
According to Al-Isfahani, which type of correspondence applies to infinite things that are together and ordered?
A) Detailed correspondence
B) General correspondence
C) Both types
D) Neither type

Key Takeaway
The proof of correspondence (burhan al-tatbiq) is valid only for infinite series that are simultaneously existent and causally ordered, using general correspondence, not detailed.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you try to understand something infinite about Allah (like His attributes), do you ever fall into the trap of seeking detailed correspondence where only general correspondence is possible? How can you train yourself to accept general correspondence?
?
In your own thinking about the chain of existence, have you ever assumed that a logical proof works for all cases, only to realize it has conditions? How does this lesson humble your intellectual confidence?
?
The proof of regress shows that every series must have a First Cause. Does your heart rest in that First Cause, or do you still feel anxiety about the infinite chain? What step can you take today to deepen your reliance on Allah as the ultimate cause?

The Condition of External Coexistence vs. Conceptual Attribution
Al-Isfahani distinguishes real and conceptual attribution in response to a coexistence objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the distinction between real and conceptual attribution and why conceptual attribution suffices for the proof of correspondence without requiring external coexistence.

Core Idea
Conceptual attribution bridges the gap when external coexistence is absent.

Al-Isfahani responds to the objection that successive series lack external coexistence. He clarifies that if the attribution of the occurrence is conceptual (intiza`i), it only requires the intellect to conceptualize the attribute from the external existence of the described thing. This distinction resolves the objection and preserves the proof.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
Read the initial objection that the proof requires external coexistence.
2
Distinguish attribution types
Notice the distinction between real (haqiqi) and conceptual (intiza`i) attribution.
Conceptual attribution is key to the response.
3
Understand the response
Al-Isfahani argues that conceptual attribution does not require external togetherness, only that the intellect can extract the attribute.
4
Apply to the proof
Reflect on how this preserves the proof of correspondence for an infinite series.
