⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( إذ ليست مجتمعة بحسب الخارج إلخ) والوقوع المذكور إذا كان عارضاً في الخارج يقتضي وجود الطرفين في الخارج معا والجواب أن الاتصاف بالوقوع المذكور إذا كان حقيقياً فالحال كما لو ذكرت وأما إذا كان انتزاعياً فلا يقتضي إلا وجود الموصوف في الخارج بحيث إذا لاحظ العقل انتزع منه الصفة والوقوع المذكور كذلك كالتعاقب فلا حاجة إلى الاجتماع وهو يكفي لنا في الاستدلال فإن كون السلسلة الغير متناهية في الخارج بحالة إذا لاحظها العقل قوله: (ليسقط عنهم ذلك النقض وجه سقوط النقض بمراتب الأعداد عندهم ليس عدمية العدد فإنه موجود عندهم، بل عدم الترتب بناء على ما هو المختار عندهم من أن كل عدد مركب من الوحدات لا الأعداد التي تحته كما سيأتي، وبهذا يظهر أن النقض على من الحكماء بجزئية بعض الأعداد من البعض، وعدم تناهي النفوس الناطقة مثلاً وارد قطعاً إلا أن يقولوا بعدمية الوحدة فافهم. من قال قوله: (إذ ليست مجتمعة بحسب الخارج في زمان أصلاً) فيه بحث، لأن الحوادث المتعاقبة وإن لم تجتمع في الوجود الخارجي لكنها مجتمعة في الوجود الظلي عندهم لكونها ثابتة في علم الملأ الأعلى لأنهم قائلون بأن علوم العقول والنفوس بحصول صور الأشياء فيها بل علم المبدأ الأول أيضاً عند الشيخ أبي علي كذلك وهذا الاجتماع كاف في جريان برهان التطبيق وانتقاض دليلهم على أصولهم لأن علم المبادي العالية بالأشياء عندهم إنما هو بسبب العلم بعللها كما صرح به الرازي في النمط السابع من المحاكمات وكل حادث جزء من علة حادث آخر فكذا علم كل واحد من الحوادث جزء من علة علم الآخر فيحصل الترتيب الطبيعي بحسب الوجود الظلي وإن فرض عدم كفاية علمها للحوادث بأوقاتها الواقعة هي فيها بالترتيب بحسب الأوقات . اللهم إلا أن يقال عبارة الرازي هكذا ثبت أن ذات المبدأ الأول علة لمعلوله وثبت أن العلم بالعلة علة العلم بالمعلول فيجوز أن يكون إطلاق العلة على العلم بالعلة بطريق المشاكلة ومراده الاستلزام فإنهم صرحوا بأن العلم التام بالعلل يستلزم العلم بالمعلول لأن العلم التام بها هو الصفات التي من جملتها العلية والعلم بالعلية لا يمكن بدون العلم بالمعلول وأما القول بأن العلم الأول علة للعلم الثاني فبعيد جداً كيف والعلم بالعلية متوقف على العلم بالمعلول ضرورة توقف معرفة الإضافة على معرفة المضافين فامتنع أن يكون موجباً وعلة له . قوله : ( وكذا لا يتم التطبيق إذا كانت الآحاد موجودة معاً ولم يكن بينها ترتب بوجه ما فيه بحث أما أولاً : فلان وقوع كل واحد من آحاد الجملة الناقصة بإزاء واحد من آحاد الجملة التامة أن يعلم ذاتها مع مالها من
His statement: '(since they are not together externally, etc.)' – and the aforementioned occurrence, if it is an accident in the external, requires the existence of both parties externally together. The answer: if the attribution of the mentioned occurrence is real, then the situation is as you mentioned; but if it is conceptual (intiza`i), it only requires the existence of the described thing in the external such that when the intellect observes, it extracts the attribute. The mentioned occurrence is like that, like succession, so there is no need for togetherness, and it suffices for us in inference, for the infinite series in the external is in a state such that when the intellect observes it... His statement: '(to refute from them that objection)' – the aspect of the refutation of the objection through ranks of numbers is, according to them, not the non-existence of number, for it exists according to them, but the lack of order, based on their chosen view that every number is composed of units, not of the numbers below it, as will come. By this it appears that the objection against those philosophers who hold the partiality of some numbers from others and the non-finiteness of rational souls, for example, is definitely valid unless they say by the non-existence of the unit, so understand. Some said: His statement: '(since they are not together externally in any time at all)' – there is discussion, because successive events, even if they do not meet in external existence, yet they are together in shadow existence (al-wujud al-zilli) according to them, because they are established in the knowledge of the highest assembly, for they hold that the knowledges of intellects and souls are by the obtaining of forms of things in them, and even the knowledge of the First Principle according to the Shaykh Abi `Ali is likewise. And this togetherness is sufficient for the application of the proof of correspondence and the refutation of their proof on their own principles, because the knowledge of the high principles of things according to them is only through knowledge of their causes, as al-Razi stated in the Seventh Pattern of al-Muhakamat. And every event is part of the cause of another event, so likewise the knowledge of each event is part of the cause of the knowledge of the other, so natural order occurs according to the shadow existence, even if it is assumed that their knowledge of events does not suffice for their times occurring in them in order according to times. Unless one says: al-Razi's phrase is this: It is established that the essence of the First Principle is a cause for its effect, and it is established that knowledge of the cause is a cause for knowledge of the effect. So it is possible that applying the term 'cause' to knowledge of the cause is by way of similitude (mushakala), and his intention is implication (istilzam). For they stated that complete knowledge of causes implies knowledge of the effect, because complete knowledge of them is the attributes which include causality, and knowledge of causality is impossible without knowledge of the effect. As for the claim that the first knowledge is a cause for the second knowledge, that is very far-fetched; how, while knowledge of causality depends on knowledge of the effect of necessity, because knowledge of the relation depends on knowledge of the two relata, so it is impossible that it be an efficient cause and a cause for it. His statement: '(and likewise the correspondence is not completed if the units exist together and there is no order between them in any way)' – there is discussion. Firstly, because the occurrence of each unit of the deficient series opposite one unit of the complete series requires that one know its essence with what it has of...
Source pages p. 177

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on several phrases, addressing objections and responses concerning the conditions for the proof of correspondence. Al-Isfahani first comments on the phrase 'since they are not together externally' (idh laysat mujtami'a bihasab al-kharij). He explains that the occurrence (wuqu`) of the pairing, if it is an external accident, requires both parties to exist externally together. The answer is: if the attribution of the occurrence is real (haqiqi), then the situation stands as stated; but if it is conceptual (intiza`i), it only requires the described thing to exist externally such that the intellect can extract the attribute. The occurrence here is like succession — no need for simultaneous togetherness, and this suffices for the inference because the infinite series in the external is in a state from which the intellect can conceptualize the correspondence. Next, he comments on the phrase 'to refute from them that objection' (li-yasqut `anhum dhalika al-naqd). He explains that the refutation of the numbers objection, according to the philosophers, is not due to the non-existence of number (since number exists for them) but due to lack of order, because every number is composed of units, not of the numbers below it. This shows that the objection against those philosophers who hold that some numbers are parts of others and that rational souls are infinite is valid, unless they deny the reality of the unit. Then he addresses the objection that successive events, though not externally coexistent, are together in shadow existence (al-wujud al-zilli) because they exist in the knowledge of the higher beings. He argues that this shadow existence is sufficient for the proof of correspondence on their own principles, since knowledge of causes implies knowledge of effects, creating a natural order. However, he then examines al-Razi's statement that knowledge of the cause is a cause for knowledge of the effect, suggesting that this is by way of similitude (mushakala) and actually implies implication (istilzam), not efficient causation. The claim that the first knowledge is a cause for the second knowledge is rejected because knowledge of causality depends on knowledge of the effect. Finally, he comments on the phrase that correspondence is not completed if units exist together without any order, noting that there is discussion. The first point is that the occurrence of each unit of the deficient series opposite one unit of the complete series requires knowledge of the essence with its attributes, as the text cuts off.

Key Terms
الانتزاع
الاجتماع الخارجي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that the proof of correspondence requires both series to exist together externally at the same time.
Correction: Al-Isfahani clarifies that conceptual attribution suffices; the intellect can conceptualize the correspondence from the external existence of one series.

Checkpoint
What type of attribution, according to Al-Isfahani, suffices for the proof of correspondence without requiring external coexistence?
Real (haqiqi)
Conceptual (intiza`i)
Both
Neither

Key Takeaway
Conceptual attribution allows the proof of correspondence to proceed even when both series are not externally coexistent.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you reflect on your belief in Allah, do you rely more on intellectual proofs like the impossibility of infinite regress, or on feelings and visible signs? How would your certainty change if you internalized the logical necessity of a First Cause?
?
In your spiritual life, are there attributes of Allah (like His mercy or power) that you struggle to feel because you don't see them externally? This lesson shows that conceptual attribution extracted from the signs of creation is valid. Will you commit to actively extracting these attributes from what you see, even when you don't feel their presence?

Refuting the Numbers Objection: Order vs. Existence
Al-Isfahani refutes the numbers objection by highlighting the lack of order.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the numbers objection fails according to the philosophers, and why order is the crucial factor.

Core Idea
The numbers objection fails because numbers exist but lack proper order, not because they are non-existent.

Al-Isfahani addresses an objection based on the ranks of numbers. Some might argue that numbers form an infinite series without external coexistence. He explains that the refutation is not due to the non-existence of number (since numbers exist) but due to the lack of order. The philosophers hold that every number is composed of units, not of the numbers below it, so there is no real ordering that violates the proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the numbers objection
The objection uses the infinite series of numbers as a counterexample.
2
Analyze the refutation
Al-Isfahani explains that the refutation is based on lack of order, not non-existence.
3
Understand the philosophers' view
Numbers are composed of units, not of other numbers, so no natural order exists.
4
Recognize the exception
If one holds that numbers are parts of others, the objection stands, unless the unit is denied.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Then he addresses the objection that successive events, though not externally coexistent, are together in shadow existence (al-wujud al-zilli) because they exist in the knowledge of the higher beings. He argues that this shadow existence is sufficient for the proof of correspondence on their own principles, since knowledge of causes implies knowledge of effects, creating a natural order. However, he then examines al-Razi's statement that knowledge of the cause is a cause for knowledge of the effect, suggesting that this is by way of similitude (mushakala) and actually implies implication (istilzam), not efficient causation. The claim that the first knowledge is a cause for the second knowledge is rejected because knowledge of causality depends on knowledge of the effect. Finally, he comments on the phrase that correspondence is not completed if units exist together without any order, noting that there is discussion. The first point is that the occurrence of each unit of the deficient series opposite one unit of the complete series requires knowledge of the essence with its attributes, as the text cuts off.

Misconception: One might think that the infinite series of numbers disproves the need for external coexistence.
Correction: Al-Isfahani shows that numbers are not a counterexample because they lack the required order.

Shadow Existence and the Sufficiency of Mental Coexistence
Al-Isfahani defends the proof using shadow existence and critiques al-Razi's causal claim.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how shadow existence (al-wujud al-zilli) provides a basis for the proof of correspondence even without external coexistence, and the critique of al-Razi's view on knowledge as cause.

Core Idea
Shadow existence in divine knowledge allows the correspondence proof to stand, but knowledge of a cause is not literally a cause of knowledge of the effect.

Al-Isfahani addresses the objection that successive events are not externally coexistent by appealing to shadow existence (al-wujud al-zilli). According to the philosophers, events exist in the knowledge of higher beings, particularly in the knowledge of the First Principle. This mental coexistence suffices for the proof. However, he then critiques al-Razi's statement that knowledge of the cause is a cause of knowledge of the effect, arguing it is merely implicative, not causal.

Guided Path
1
Read the shadow existence argument
Successive events coexist in shadow existence (divine knowledge).
2
See how it suffices for the proof
Knowledge of causes creates a natural order in shadow existence.
3
Examine al-Razi's statement
Al-Razi said knowledge of the cause is a cause for knowledge of the effect.
4
Understand the critique
Al-Isfahani argues this is metaphorical; knowledge of the cause implies, not causes, knowledge of the effect.
5
Note the dependency
Knowledge of causality depends on knowledge of the effect, so literal causation is impossible.

His statement: '(since they are not together externally, etc.)' – and the aforementioned occurrence, if it is an accident in the external, requires the existence of both parties externally together. The answer: if the attribution of the mentioned occurrence is real, then the situation is as you mentioned; but if it is conceptual (intiza`i), it only requires the existence of the described thing in the external such that when the intellect observes, it extracts the attribute. The mentioned occurrence is like that, like succession, so there is no need for togetherness, and it suffices for us in inference, for the infinite series in the external is in a state such that when the intellect observes it... And every event is part of the cause of another event, so likewise the knowledge of each event is part of the cause of the knowledge of the other, so natural order occurs according to the shadow existence, even if it is assumed that their knowledge of events does not suffice for their times occurring in them in order according to times. Unless one says: al-Razi's phrase is this: It is established that the essence of the First Principle is a cause for its effect, and it is established that knowledge of the cause is a cause for knowledge of the effect. So it is possible that applying the term 'cause' to knowledge of the cause is by way of similitude (mushakala), and his intention is implication (istilzam). For they stated that complete knowledge of causes implies knowledge of the effect, because complete knowledge of them is the attributes which include causality, and knowledge of causality is impossible without knowledge of the effect. As for the claim that the first knowledge is a cause for the second knowledge, that is very far-fetched; how, while knowledge of causality depends on knowledge of the effect of necessity, because knowledge of the relation depends on knowledge of the two relata, so it is impossible that it be an efficient cause and a cause for it. His statement: '(and likewise the correspondence is not completed if the units exist together and there is no order between them in any way)' – there is discussion. Firstly, because the occurrence of each unit of the deficient series opposite one unit of the complete series requires that one know its essence with what it has of...

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on several phrases, addressing objections and responses concerning the conditions for the proof of correspondence. Al-Isfahani first comments on the phrase 'since they are not together externally' (idh laysat mujtami'a bihasab al-kharij). He explains that the occurrence (wuqu`) of the pairing, if it is an external accident, requires both parties to exist externally together. The answer is: if the attribution of the occurrence is real (haqiqi), then the situation stands as stated; but if it is conceptual (intiza`i), it only requires the described thing to exist externally such that the intellect can extract the attribute. The occurrence here is like succession — no need for simultaneous togetherness, and this suffices for the inference because the infinite series in the external is in a state from which the intellect can conceptualize the correspondence. Next, he comments on the phrase 'to refute from them that objection' (li-yasqut `anhum dhalika al-naqd). He explains that the refutation of the numbers objection, according to the philosophers, is not due to the non-existence of number (since number exists for them) but due to lack of order, because every number is composed of units, not of the numbers below it. This shows that the objection against those philosophers who hold that some numbers are parts of others and that rational souls are infinite is valid, unless they deny the reality of the unit. Then he addresses the objection that successive events, though not externally coexistent, are together in shadow existence (al-wujud al-zilli) because they exist in the knowledge of the higher beings. He argues that this shadow existence is sufficient for the proof of correspondence on their own principles, since knowledge of causes implies knowledge of effects, creating a natural order. However, he then examines al-Razi's statement that knowledge of the cause is a cause for knowledge of the effect, suggesting that this is by way of similitude (mushakala) and actually implies implication (istilzam), not efficient causation. The claim that the first knowledge is a cause for the second knowledge is rejected because knowledge of causality depends on knowledge of the effect. Finally, he comments on the phrase that correspondence is not completed if units exist together without any order, noting that there is discussion. The first point is that the occurrence of each unit of the deficient series opposite one unit of the complete series requires knowledge of the essence with its attributes, as the text cuts off.

الاستلزام

Correction: Al-Isfahani shows that shadow existence, as knowledge in the divine mind, is sufficient to establish the required order.

Objection: Shadowy Existence in Divine Knowledge
Objection that shadowy coexistence suffices for Burhan al-Tatbiq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the objection that shadowy coexistence in the knowledge of higher beings suffices for the Burhan al-Tatbiq.

Core Idea
Shadowy coexistence in divine knowledge is claimed to invalidate the proof.

This lesson presents an objection raised against the earlier argument. The opponent argues that even if the two series do not coexist externally, they coexist in the shadowy existence in the knowledge of the intellects and the First Principle. According to their principles, this shadowy coexistence should be enough for the Burhan al-Tatbiq to apply, thus refuting the Ash‘ari position.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
Read the Arabic passage carefully, then its translation. Notice how the opponent builds the argument on the principle that knowledge of causes implies knowledge of effects.
The key term 'shadowy existence' (الوجود الظلي) refers to mental or intelligible existence.
2
Understand the role of shadowy existence
The opponent claims that the two series (the successive events) do not need to coexist externally; their coexistence in the knowledge of higher beings is sufficient. This is because, according to their principles, knowledge of the cause entails knowledge of the effect, creating a natural order in the shadowy realm.
3
Note the reference to al-Razi
The opponent cites al-Razi's statement from al-Muhakamat to support the idea that knowledge of higher principles is due to knowledge of causes. This sets up the refutation in the next lesson.

المتعاقبة وإن لم تجتمع في الوجود الخارجي لكنها مجتمعة في الوجود الظلي عندهم لكونها ثابتة في علم الملأ الأعلى لأنهم قائلون بأن علوم العقول والنفوس بحصول صور الأشياء فيها بل علم المبدأ الأول أيضاً عند الشيخ أبي علي كذلك وهذا الاجتماع كاف في جريان برهان التطبيق وانتقاض دليلهم على أصولهم لأن علم المبادي العالية بالأشياء عندهم إنما هو بسبب العلم بعللها كما صرح به الرازي في النمط السابع من المحاكمات وكل حادث جزء من علة حادث آخر فكذا علم كل واحد من الحوادث جزء من علة علم الآخر فيحصل الترتيب الطبيعي بحسب الوجود الظلي وإن فرض عدم كفاية علمها للحوادث بأوقاتها الواقعة هي فيها بالترتيب بحسب الأوقات . اللهم إلا أن يقال عبارة الرازي هكذا ثبت أن ذات المبدأ الأول علة لمعلوله وثبت أن العلم بالعلة علة العلم بالمعلول فيجوز أن يكون إطلاق العلة على العلم بالعلة بطريق المشاكلة ومراده الاستلزام فإنهم صرحوا بأن العلم التام بالعلل يستلزم العلم بالمعلول لأن العلم التام بها هو الصفات التي من جملتها العلية والعلم بالعلية لا يمكن بدون العلم بالمعلول وأما القول بأن العلم الأول علة للعلم الثاني فبعيد جداً كيف والعلم بالعلية متوقف على العلم بالمعلول ضرورة توقف معرفة الإضافة على معرفة المضافين فامتنع أن يكون موجبا وعلة له .
The successive [series], even if they do not coexist in external existence, yet they are coexistent in shadowy existence according to them, because they are established in the knowledge of the supreme assembly, for they hold that the knowledges of the intellects and souls occur by the obtaining of forms of things in them. Even the knowledge of the First Principle according to Shaykh Abu Ali is also like that. And this coexistence is sufficient for the running of the Burhan al-Tatbiq and the invalidation of their proof according to their own principles, because the knowledge of the higher principles of things according to them is only due to the knowledge of their causes, as al-Razi stated in the Seventh Pattern of al-Muhakamat. And every event is part of the cause of another event, so likewise the knowledge of each event is part of the cause of the knowledge of the other; thus natural order occurs according to shadowy existence, even if one supposes the inadequacy of its knowledge of events at their specific times in temporal order. However, it could be said that al-Razi's expression is as follows: it is established that the essence of the First Principle is the cause of its effect, and it is established that knowledge of the cause is the cause of knowledge of the effect. So it is possible that the application of 'cause' to the knowledge of the cause is by way of similitude and his intention is implication. For they stated that complete knowledge of causes implies knowledge of the effect, because complete knowledge of them is the attributes which include causality, and knowledge of causality cannot be without knowledge of the effect. As for the saying that the first knowledge is a cause for the second knowledge, it is very far, because knowledge of causality depends on knowledge of the effect necessarily, as knowledge of the relation depends on knowledge of the two relata; so it is impossible that it be a cause and an efficient cause for it.

Commentary
This passage presents an objection from those who claim that even if the series do not coexist externally, they coexist in the shadowy existence (الوجود الظلي) in the knowledge of higher beings (the intellects and the First Principle). According to their principles, this shadowy coexistence should suffice for the Burhan al-Tatbiq because knowledge of causes implies knowledge of effects, creating a natural order. The author then considers a possible counter-response based on al-Razi's words: al-Razi said that knowledge of the cause is a cause of knowledge of the effect, but this might be metaphorical (مشاكلة) meaning implication (استلزام), not efficient causality. The author argues that the claim that the first knowledge is a cause of the second is untenable because knowledge of causality depends on knowledge of the effect, as the relation (causality) requires both relata (cause and effect). Thus, the first knowledge cannot be a cause of the second, and the shadowy coexistence argument fails.

Refutation: Knowledge of Causality Requires Knowledge of Effect
Refutation based on dependency of knowledge of causality

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the shadowy existence argument fails: because knowledge of the cause does not efficiently cause knowledge of the effect due to the dependency of causality on both relata.

Core Idea
Knowledge of causality depends on knowledge of the effect, not the other way around.

The opponent's reliance on shadowy existence is refuted by a careful analysis of the relationship between knowledge of cause and knowledge of effect. Al-Razi's words are examined, showing that he meant implication, not efficient causality. The dependency of causality on both relata makes it impossible for the first knowledge to be a cause of the second.

Guided Path
1
Read the refutation
Read the Arabic passage and translation. The author presents a counter-argument by reinterpreting al-Razi's statement.
Key terms: المشاكلة (similitude) and الاستلزام (implication).
2
Analyze al-Razi's expression
Al-Razi said that knowledge of the cause is the cause of knowledge of the effect. The author suggests this might be metaphorical (مشاكلة), meaning implication, not efficient causality.
The word 'cause' here might be used loosely.
3
Understand the distinction between cause and implication
Complete knowledge of causes implies knowledge of the effect, but it does not efficiently cause it. Knowledge of causality includes the attributes of the cause, which cannot be known without knowing the effect.
4
Grasp the dependency argument
Knowledge of causality depends on knowledge of the effect because the relation (causality) requires both the cause and the effect. Therefore, the first knowledge cannot be a cause of the second.
This refutes the shadowy existence argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المتعاقبة وإن لم تجتمع في الوجود الخارجي لكنها مجتمعة في الوجود الظلي عندهم لكونها ثابتة في علم الملأ الأعلى لأنهم قائلون بأن علوم العقول والنفوس بحصول صور الأشياء فيها بل علم المبدأ الأول أيضاً عند الشيخ أبي علي كذلك وهذا الاجتماع كاف في جريان برهان التطبيق وانتقاض دليلهم على أصولهم لأن علم المبادي العالية بالأشياء عندهم إنما هو بسبب العلم بعللها كما صرح به الرازي في النمط السابع من المحاكمات وكل حادث جزء من علة حادث آخر فكذا علم كل واحد من الحوادث جزء من علة علم الآخر فيحصل الترتيب الطبيعي بحسب الوجود الظلي وإن فرض عدم كفاية علمها للحوادث بأوقاتها الواقعة هي فيها بالترتيب بحسب الأوقات . اللهم إلا أن يقال عبارة الرازي هكذا ثبت أن ذات المبدأ الأول علة لمعلوله وثبت أن العلم بالعلة علة العلم بالمعلول فيجوز أن يكون إطلاق العلة على العلم بالعلة بطريق المشاكلة ومراده الاستلزام فإنهم صرحوا بأن العلم التام بالعلل يستلزم العلم بالمعلول لأن العلم التام بها هو الصفات التي من جملتها العلية والعلم بالعلية لا يمكن بدون العلم بالمعلول وأما القول بأن العلم الأول علة للعلم الثاني فبعيد جداً كيف والعلم بالعلية متوقف على العلم بالمعلول ضرورة توقف معرفة الإضافة على معرفة المضافين فامتنع أن يكون موجبا وعلة له .
The successive [series], even if they do not coexist in external existence, yet they are coexistent in shadowy existence according to them, because they are established in the knowledge of the supreme assembly, for they hold that the knowledges of the intellects and souls occur by the obtaining of forms of things in them. Even the knowledge of the First Principle according to Shaykh Abu Ali is also like that. And this coexistence is sufficient for the running of the Burhan al-Tatbiq and the invalidation of their proof according to their own principles, because the knowledge of the higher principles of things according to them is only due to the knowledge of their causes, as al-Razi stated in the Seventh Pattern of al-Muhakamat. And every event is part of the cause of another event, so likewise the knowledge of each event is part of the cause of the knowledge of the other; thus natural order occurs according to shadowy existence, even if one supposes the inadequacy of its knowledge of events at their specific times in temporal order. However, it could be said that al-Razi's expression is as follows: it is established that the essence of the First Principle is the cause of its effect, and it is established that knowledge of the cause is the cause of knowledge of the effect. So it is possible that the application of 'cause' to the knowledge of the cause is by way of similitude and his intention is implication. For they stated that complete knowledge of causes implies knowledge of the effect, because complete knowledge of them is the attributes which include causality, and knowledge of causality cannot be without knowledge of the effect. As for the saying that the first knowledge is a cause for the second knowledge, it is very far, because knowledge of causality depends on knowledge of the effect necessarily, as knowledge of the relation depends on knowledge of the two relata; so it is impossible that it be a cause and an efficient cause for it.
Source pages p. 178

Commentary
This passage presents an objection from those who claim that even if the series do not coexist externally, they coexist in the shadowy existence (الوجود الظلي) in the knowledge of higher beings (the intellects and the First Principle). According to their principles, this shadowy coexistence should suffice for the Burhan al-Tatbiq because knowledge of causes implies knowledge of effects, creating a natural order. The author then considers a possible counter-response based on al-Razi's words: al-Razi said that knowledge of the cause is a cause of knowledge of the effect, but this might be metaphorical (مشاكلة) meaning implication (استلزام), not efficient causality. The author argues that the claim that the first knowledge is a cause of the second is untenable because knowledge of causality depends on knowledge of the effect, as the relation (causality) requires both relata (cause and effect). Thus, the first knowledge cannot be a cause of the second, and the shadowy coexistence argument fails.

Key Terms
المشاكلة
الاستلزام
العلية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Knowledge of the cause efficiently causes knowledge of the effect.
Correction: The author argues that this is metaphorical; true knowledge of causality requires prior knowledge of the effect, so it cannot be efficient causality.

Checkpoint
Why does the author say that the first knowledge cannot be a cause of the second knowledge?
A) Because the first knowledge is incomplete
B) Because knowledge of causality depends on knowledge of the effect, as a relation requires both relata
C) Because the second knowledge is prior in time
D) Because al-Razi explicitly denied it

Key Takeaway
The shadowy existence argument fails because knowledge of the cause does not efficiently cause knowledge of the effect; rather, causality requires prior knowledge of the effect, making the first knowledge dependent on the second.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you claim to have deep understanding of a cause (e.g., why a trial befell you), is it possible that you are unaware of your dependence on knowing the full effect? How would it change your attitude if you realized that your knowledge of causality is incomplete without the effect?
?
The author argues that knowledge of causality requires knowledge of the effect. Have you ever assumed you understood a cause simply by reasoning, without waiting to see its actual outcome? What might that reveal about your intellectual humility?
?
If knowledge of the cause does not efficiently produce knowledge of the effect, then your intellectual journey cannot be a simple chain of deductions. Are you willing to accept that some knowledge must be acquired through experience or revelation rather than pure reasoning? What does that imply for how you seek truth about your Creator?

The Third Proof: Bounded Distance Implies Finite Series
Third proof: finitude of distance between effect and each cause

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the third proof against infinite regress: that the distance between a given effect and each cause in a series is finite because it is bounded, implying the entire series must be finite.

Core Idea
What is bounded on both sides cannot be infinite.

The third proof uses a simple geometric intuition: if you have an effect and a cause, the 'distance' between them is enclosed by them. In an infinite chain, each cause is assumed, but that distance remains finite because it is always between two terms. This lesson unpacks that argument and its logical conditions.

Guided Path
1
Understand the structure of the proof
Read the Arabic and translation to see how the proof is presented: it claims that the distance between the effect and each cause is finite because bounded by two enclosers.
The proof relies on the concept of boundedness.
2
Examine the condition about two series
Note the condition that the two series must be possible and assumed as actual together. The intellect can assume them as actual without detailing individuals.
This condition is crucial for the proof to work.
3
Reflect on the conclusion
If each distance is finite, then the whole series is finite, because there is no infinite stretch between any cause and the effect.
This refutes the possibility of an actual infinite regress of causes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الوجه الثالث ما بين هذا المعلول المعين وكل علة من العلل الواقعة في السلسلة التي فرضت غير متناهية متناه لأنه محصور بين حاصرين هما هذا المعلول وتلك العلة ومن المحال أن يكون ما لا يتناهى محصوراً بين أمرين يحيطان به فيكون الكل أي كل السلسلة متناهياً إذا كانت الجملتان موجودتين معاً من الأمور الممكنة وإن لم يكن بين آحادهما ترتب والعقل يفرض ذلك الممكن واقعاً حتى يظهر الخلف ولا يحتاج ذلك الفرض إلى ملاحظة آحادهما مفصلة بل يكفي في فرض وقوع هذا الممكن ملاحظتها إجمالاً، فالترتب مما لا يحتاج إليه في إجراء البرهان. وأما ثانيا فلان عقولنا وإن كانت لا تقدر على استحضار ما لا نهاية له مفصلة إلا أن القوى العالية وافية بملاحظتها وتطبيقها فيرد الإشكال وأما ثالثاً فلان الجملتين إن لزم كونهما متحققتين في نفس الأمر بحيث يحصل التطبيق بينهما فيها، لم يتم الدليل لأنه لا يلزم استحالة وجود سلسلة واحدة غير متناهية . إذ ليس هناك جملتان متحققتان في نفس الأمر متطابقتان لتوقف ذلك على تباين الجملتين وانفصالهما والجزء مع الكل ليس كذلك وحديث الجبلين والرمل الذي أورده للتوضيح ضائع إذ لا مناسبة له بما نحن بصدده. وإن كفى كون الجملتين والتطبيق بينهما فرضيات محضة فالدليل جار في غير المرتب بل في مراتب الأعداد أيضاً وهذا الثالث وارد على المتكلمين أيضاً في مراتب الأعداد. قوله : ( ما بين هذا المعلول المعين وكل علة متناه لا يخلو عن مسامحة إذ لا شيء بين المعلول الأخير والعلة القريبة حتى يحكم بأنه متناه
The third aspect: What is between this specific effect and every cause among the causes occurring in the series that is assumed to be infinite is finite, because it is enclosed between two enclosers, namely this effect and that cause. And it is impossible for the infinite to be enclosed between two things that surround it; therefore the whole, i.e., the entire series, is finite. If the two series exist together among possible things, even if there is no order between their individuals, and the intellect assumes that possible as actual so that the contradiction appears, then that assumption does not require the observation of its individuals in detail; rather, in assuming the occurrence of this possible, it suffices to observe them in summary. So order is not needed for the proof. Second: Our intellects, even if they cannot summon the infinite in detail, yet the higher powers are sufficient to observe them and align them, so the problem arises. Third: If it is necessary that the two series be actualized in reality such that the alignment occurs between them, then the proof is not established because it does not necessitate the impossibility of a single infinite series; for there are not two series actualized in reality that correspond, because that depends on the distinction and separation of the two series, and the part with the whole is not like that. And the talk of the two mountains and sand which he brought for clarification is wasted, for there is no relevance to what we are about. And if it suffices that the two series and the alignment between them are purely hypothetical, then the proof applies to the non-ordered, indeed to the ranks of numbers as well. And this third [point] applies to the theologians also in the ranks of numbers. His saying: (What is between this specific effect and every cause is finite) is not free from looseness, for there is nothing between the last effect and the proximate cause for one to judge that it is finite.
Source pages p. 179

Commentary
This passage presents the third proof (الوجه الثالث) for the impossibility of infinite regress. It argues that the distance between a given effect and each cause in an assumed infinite series is finite because it is bounded by the effect and that cause. Therefore, the entire series must be finite. It then discusses the conditions for the proof: the two series must exist together among possibles; the intellect can assume that possible as actual without detailing individuals. The proof does not require order. Then it repeats the second and third sub-objections from earlier (perhaps as part of the commentary). Finally, a comment on the expression 'what is between this specific effect and every cause' is noted as imprecise (مسامحة) because there is nothing between the last effect and the proximate cause to measure. This lesson combines the proof and a critical comment.

المعلول
العلة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The third proof measures physical distance in time.
Correction: The proof uses logical boundedness, not temporal or spatial distance.

Checkpoint
What is the main claim of the third proof?
A) The series is infinite because there is no bound
B) The distance between the effect and each cause is finite, so the whole series is finite
C) The series is finite only if ordered
D) The series is infinite because causes are infinite

Key Takeaway
The third proof shows that if every segment between an effect and a cause is finite, then the entire causal chain cannot be infinite.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This proof shows that what is bounded cannot be infinite. Your life is bounded by birth and death, by time and space. How does the finitude of your own existence press you to consider what lies beyond it? Will you today acknowledge the First Cause who is not bounded?
?
The proof does not require detailed enumeration of causes; a summary conclusion suffices. Are you avoiding the ultimate conclusion about God's existence by getting lost in secondary causes and details? Will you accept the clear summary evidence and respond?
?
Every segment of the causal chain is finite—including your own choices and dependencies. Is there an area in your life where you have implicitly assumed an infinite regress of excuses or blame? Will you cut through that regress today and take responsibility before your Creator?

Objections to the Third Proof and a Refinement
Objections and critique on the third proof's wording

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the objections raised against the third proof and the critical comment on its wording.

Core Idea
Even if our minds cannot grasp the infinite, higher powers can; and if the series alignment is hypothetical, the proof works universally.

The third proof faces several issues. First, how can we assume an infinite series if our intellects cannot grasp it? The answer invokes higher powers. Second, if the two series must be actual, then the proof fails because an actual infinite series could still be one series. The third objection critiques the wording: there is no 'between' the effect and its proximate cause. This lesson unpacks these subtleties.

Guided Path
1
Read the objections
Read the Arabic for the second and third points. Note how each presents a problem to the proof.
2
Understand the higher powers response
The objection says our minds cannot handle infinite detail; the response says higher powers (angels or Allah) can.
This shifts the epistemic burden.
3
Analyze the actual vs hypothetical condition
If the two series must be actual in reality, then the proof fails because an actual infinite series could exist singly (not two). But if hypothetical, the proof applies even to numbers.
This shows the proof's strength under hypothetical assumption.
4
Examine the critique of wording
The final comment notes that saying 'what is between the effect and each cause' is imprecise because there is nothing between the last effect and its immediate cause.
This is a terminological refinement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

The Bounding Argument for Finite Causality
Jurjani presents the bounding argument for finitude of a cause chain.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Jurjani's bounding argument: a chain of causes from a chosen cause to the final effect is necessarily finite.

Core Idea
A cause chain bounded by a fixed cause and effect must be finite.

Here, al-Jurjani presents a key proof against infinite regress of causes. By focusing on the interval between a chosen cause and the final effect, he shows that the whole chain is finite. This argument is foundational for kalam's understanding of contingency and creation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic source and its translation. Notice how Jurjani sets up the proof with a conditional structure.
Pay attention to the phrase 'لا يزيد على ذلك إلا بواحد' - 'does not exceed that except by one'.
2
Identify the fixed endpoints
The argument considers a specific cause from the chain and the last effect. Everything between them is finite because it is bounded by these two points.
3
Understand the incremental addition
The whole chain from that cause to the effect is exactly that finite interval plus exactly one more cause (the chosen cause itself). So the whole is finite.
This is the core logical move: adding one to a finite set yields a finite set.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
Why does this prove infinite regress is impossible? Because any infinite chain would have to contain a segment that is not bounded in this way, but the argument shows any such segment is finite.
This connects to the broader theological objective: the created order depends on a First Cause.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المرصد الخامس - المقصد الثامن : التسلسل محال أن يستند الممكن إلى علة أيضاً ( لأنه ( أي الكل ( لا يزيد على ذلك ) أي على الواقع بين هذا المعلول وبين علة ما من تلك العلل (إلا) بواحد ( من جانب العلل فإن ما عدا الواحد في هذا الجانب يكون واقعاً بينه وبين ذلك المعلول الأخير وإذا كان الواقع بينهما متناهياً ولا شك أن الكل لا يزيد في هذا الجانب على ذلك الواقع إلا بواحدة فقط كان الكل الذي لا يزيد على المتناهي إلا بواحد متناهياً وليس ما ذكره من قبيل ما يقال إن ما بين (ا) و (ب) أقل من ذراع وما بين (ب) و (ج) أقل منها وما بين (ج) و (د) كذلك فيكون ما بين (۱) و (د) أقل من ذراع فإنه ظاهر الفساد بل هو من قبيل أن يقال ما بين (ا) و (ب) أقل من ذراع وما بين (ا) و (د) كذلك فإذا أخذ (د) مع الواقع بينه وبين (ا) لم يزد على ما هو أقل من ذراع إلا بنقطة (د) وهذا حكم صحيح ( فإنه إذا هذا الجزء ( المعين ( من المسافة وكل جزء منها ( لا يزيد على فرسخ يكون المجموع ) أي مجموع المسافة ) لا يزيد على فرسخ إلا بجزء ) واحد ( ضرورة) والمراد أن المجموع لو زاد عليه لم يزد إلا بجزء واحد وذلك لأن زيادتها عليه بالجزء. وما لا يزيد على المتناهي إلا بواحد أو بعدد متناه فهو متناه بالضرورة
The fifth viewpoint - the eighth objective: Infinite regress is impossible. That a contingent thing is based on a cause is also impossible because it (i.e., the whole) does not exceed that (i.e., that which lies between this effect and some one of those causes) except by one (from the side of the causes. For everything other than that one in this side lies between it and that last effect. And when that which lies between them is finite, and there is no doubt that the whole does not exceed in this side that which lies between them except by one only, then the whole, which does not exceed the finite except by one, is finite. And what he mentioned is not of the type of what is said: 'That which is between (a) and (b) is less than a cubit, and what is between (b) and (c) is less than it, and what is between (c) and (d) is likewise, so that which is between (a) and (d) is less than a cubit'—for that is evidently corrupt. Rather it is of the type of what is said: 'That which is between (a) and (b) is less than a cubit, and that which is between (a) and (d) is likewise; so if (d) is taken together with that which lies between it and (a), it does not exceed what is less than a cubit except by the point (d).' And this is a correct judgment. For if this specific part of the distance and every part of it does not exceed a parasang, then the total (i.e., the total distance) does not exceed a parasang except by one part, necessarily. And what is meant is that if the total were to exceed it, it would not exceed except by one part, because its excess over it is by the part. And that which does not exceed the finite except by one or by a finite number is finite, necessarily.
Source pages p. 180

Commentary
This passage is a proof that an infinite regress of causes is impossible. The author, al-Jurjani, presents a bounding argument: consider a chain of causes leading to a specific effect. Pick one particular cause in that chain (any one). Everything between that cause and the last effect is finite in number because it is bounded by that cause and the effect. The whole chain from that cause to the effect does not exceed that finite interval except by one additional term (the chosen cause itself). Therefore, the whole chain from that cause to the effect is finite. The author then distinguishes this correct reasoning from a flawed analogy involving distances: if you have intervals each less than a cubit, it does not follow that the sum is less than a cubit. The correct analogy is when you fix a single starting point: e.g., the interval from (a) to (b) is less than a cubit, and from (a) to (d) is also less—then adding (d) only adds a point, not a whole interval. He compares this to a distance where each part is less than a parasang; the total is at most one parasang plus one part. The conclusion: any whole that exceeds the finite by only one or a finite number is itself finite.

Key Terms
تسلسل
علة
متناهٍ

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that even if the interval between a cause and effect is finite, adding one more cause could still lead to an infinite chain if the chain extends indefinitely in the other direction.
Correction: The argument does not consider the entire infinite regress; it only shows that any segment between a specific cause and the last effect is finite. This is sufficient to break the regress because if the segment is finite, the regress cannot be infinite.

Checkpoint
What is the main reason the whole chain from the chosen cause to the last effect is finite?
A) The interval between them is infinite.
B) The whole is the finite interval plus one, and adding one to a finite yields a finite.
C) The chosen cause is infinite.
D) The last effect is infinite.

Key Takeaway
Any chain of causes bounded by a fixed cause and a last effect is necessarily finite.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If every causal chain in your life is bounded, and you cannot escape having a first cause, then what does that demand of you right now? Are you living as if your deeds have no ultimate consequence, or are you acknowledging the first cause that holds every moment?
?
Consider the last effect in your life—a sin you committed or a blessing you received. Trace its cause chain. Does it eventually lead back to Allah? If so, how does that change your attitude toward that event today?
?
The argument shows that any bounded chain must be finite. Your life is bounded by birth and death. Does your daily pursuits reflect that your causal chain is finite, or do you act as if you have infinite time? What will you change today to live in light of that finitude?

Correct Analogy for the Bounding Argument
Jurjani distinguishes his correct analogy from a flawed one and states the general principle.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will distinguish Jurjani's correct analogy from a flawed one, and understand the general principle: anything that exceeds the finite only by a finite number is itself finite.

Core Idea
Exceeding the finite by only one or a finite number yields finitude.

After presenting the bounding argument, Jurjani clarifies it with a distance analogy. He contrasts his correct reasoning with a flawed one that would lead to an erroneous conclusion. This lesson unpacks the analogy and how it reinforces the proof.

Guided Path
1
Read the analogy section
Read the Arabic for the flawed and correct analogies. Notice the difference: in the flawed one, intervals are not anchored to a common point.
The flawed analogy: (a-b) < cubit, (b-c) < cubit, (c-d) < cubit does not imply (a-d) < cubit.
2
Understand the correct analogy
In the correct analogy, (a-b) < cubit and (a-d) < cubit. Then adding d to the interval (a-d) only adds point d, not a whole interval, so the total is less than cubit+point.
The key is that the interval (a-d) is already bounded and less than a cubit.
3
Generalize to the cause chain
Just as the total distance does not exceed a parasang plus one part, the cause chain does not exceed the finite interval plus one cause. Thus the whole is finite.
4
State the universal principle
The final sentence gives the general rule: anything that does not exceed the finite except by one or a finite number is itself finite. This is the logical foundation of the argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المرصد الخامس - المقصد الثامن : التسلسل محال أن يستند الممكن إلى علة أيضاً ( لأنه ( أي الكل ( لا يزيد على ذلك ) أي على الواقع بين هذا المعلول وبين علة ما من تلك العلل (إلا) بواحد ( من جانب العلل فإن ما عدا الواحد في هذا الجانب يكون واقعاً بينه وبين ذلك المعلول الأخير وإذا كان الواقع بينهما متناهياً ولا شك أن الكل لا يزيد في هذا الجانب على ذلك الواقع إلا بواحدة فقط كان الكل الذي لا يزيد على المتناهي إلا بواحد متناهياً وليس ما ذكره من قبيل ما يقال إن ما بين (ا) و (ب) أقل من ذراع وما بين (ب) و (ج) أقل منها وما بين (ج) و (د) كذلك فيكون ما بين (۱) و (د) أقل من ذراع فإنه ظاهر الفساد بل هو من قبيل أن يقال ما بين (ا) و (ب) أقل من ذراع وما بين (ا) و (د) كذلك فإذا أخذ (د) مع الواقع بينه وبين (ا) لم يزد على ما هو أقل من ذراع إلا بنقطة (د) وهذا حكم صحيح ( فإنه إذا هذا الجزء ( المعين ( من المسافة وكل جزء منها ( لا يزيد على فرسخ يكون المجموع ) أي مجموع المسافة ) لا يزيد على فرسخ إلا بجزء ) واحد ( ضرورة) والمراد أن المجموع لو زاد عليه لم يزد إلا بجزء واحد وذلك لأن زيادتها عليه بالجزء. وما لا يزيد على المتناهي إلا بواحد أو بعدد متناه فهو متناه بالضرورة
The fifth viewpoint - the eighth objective: Infinite regress is impossible. That a contingent thing is based on a cause is also impossible because it (i.e., the whole) does not exceed that (i.e., that which lies between this effect and some one of those causes) except by one (from the side of the causes. For everything other than that one in this side lies between it and that last effect. And when that which lies between them is finite, and there is no doubt that the whole does not exceed in this side that which lies between them except by one only, then the whole, which does not exceed the finite except by one, is finite. And what he mentioned is not of the type of what is said: 'That which is between (a) and (b) is less than a cubit, and what is between (b) and (c) is less than it, and what is between (c) and (d) is likewise, so that which is between (a) and (d) is less than a cubit'—for that is evidently corrupt. Rather it is of the type of what is said: 'That which is between (a) and (b) is less than a cubit, and that which is between (a) and (d) is likewise; so if (d) is taken together with that which lies between it and (a), it does not exceed what is less than a cubit except by the point (d).' And this is a correct judgment. For if this specific part of the distance and every part of it does not exceed a parasang, then the total (i.e., the total distance) does not exceed a parasang except by one part, necessarily. And what is meant is that if the total were to exceed it, it would not exceed except by one part, because its excess over it is by the part. And that which does not exceed the finite except by one or by a finite number is finite, necessarily.
Source pages p. 180

Commentary
This passage is a proof that an infinite regress of causes is impossible. The author, al-Jurjani, presents a bounding argument: consider a chain of causes leading to a specific effect. Pick one particular cause in that chain (any one). Everything between that cause and the last effect is finite in number because it is bounded by that cause and the effect. The whole chain from that cause to the effect does not exceed that finite interval except by one additional term (the chosen cause itself). Therefore, the whole chain from that cause to the effect is finite. The author then distinguishes this correct reasoning from a flawed analogy involving distances: if you have intervals each less than a cubit, it does not follow that the sum is less than a cubit. The correct analogy is when you fix a single starting point: e.g., the interval from (a) to (b) is less than a cubit, and from (a) to (d) is also less—then adding (d) only adds a point, not a whole interval. He compares this to a distance where each part is less than a parasang; the total is at most one parasang plus one part. The conclusion: any whole that exceeds the finite by only one or a finite number is itself finite.

Key Terms
ذراع (cubit)
فرسخ (parasang)
جزء (part)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that if each individual cause-effect link is finite, the entire infinite chain is also finite. This is like the flawed analogy.
Correction: The correct analogy shows that the whole is finite only when the interval is anchored at a fixed starting point. The flawed analogy would allow infinite accumulation.

Checkpoint
In the correct analogy, what is added to the interval (a-d) when taking d together with it?
A) The whole interval (a-d)
B) The point d only
C) The interval (b-c)
D) A cubit

Key Takeaway
Finitude is preserved when the whole exceeds the finite only by a single or finite addition.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you contemplate the fact that the universe is finite and limited, does it humble your heart or make you feel distant from Allah? How does this logical certainty shape your daily gratitude for His boundlessness?
?
Reflect on a time you used flawed reasoning to justify a sin or a doubt. How does Jurjani's insistence on precise analogy challenge you to examine the foundations of your own beliefs? Will you commit to seeking truth with the same rigor?
?
If the infinite chain of causes must end in a Finite Creator, why do you still sometimes live as if this world has no endpoint? What one change can you make today to live in light of the finite nature of all things but the Face of Allah?

Suhrawardī's Admission: The Bounding Proof is Intuitive
Suhrawardī admits the bounding proof is intuitive, not purely demonstrative.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Suhrawardī considers the bounding proof intuitive rather than purely demonstrative, and how intuitive insight resolves the problem of an infinite causal series.

Core Idea
Intuitive insight finds the bounding cause where pure reason cannot.

Suhrawardī, the Illuminationist philosopher, adduced a famous argument for the finitude of causal series known as the 'Throne proof.' In this passage, he makes a remarkable admission: the proof is not purely demonstrative but depends on intuitive power. He explains why ordinary reasoning cannot identify the bounding term in an infinite series, yet the intuitive knower can grasp it. This lesson unpacks that admission and its implications for the nature of the proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the admission
Suhrawardī explicitly states that the proof is intuitive (ḥadsī), not purely demonstrative. Note the term 'Throne proof' and who he is referring to (the author of al-Ishrāq, i.e., himself).
This admission is crucial—it acknowledges a limitation of pure reason.
2
Understand the problem with infinite series
If the causes were finite, it would be obvious which cause bounds the series. But if they are infinite, every cause has a preceding cause, so no single cause can be pointed out as the boundary.
This is the core challenge: infinite regress makes the bounding term invisible to ordinary reasoning.
3
The intuitive solution
Despite this, the possessor of intuitive power (al-quwwa al-ḥadsīyya) knows that there is a certain bounding cause, even if it cannot be specifically identified. That cause, together with the last effect, encompasses everything between them.
Intuition grasps what demonstration cannot capture.
4
Reflect on the nature of the proof
This shows that the Throne proof relies on a faculty beyond pure logical inference. It is not a failure but a recognition of the distinct role of intuitive insight in metaphysics.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعترف من احتج به وسماه برهاناً عرشياً وهو صاحب الإشراق بأنه حدسي محتاج إلى حدس ليعلم به صحته وذلك لأن العلل لو كانت متناهية لظهر ظهوراً تاماً أن ما عدا واحدة معينة منها واقع بينها وبين المعلول الأخير وأما إذا فرضت غير متناهية كما فيما نحن بصدده فليس يظهر هذا المعنى فيه إذ لا يتصور هناك واحدة من العلل إلا وقبلها علة أخرى فكيف يتصور الانحصار لكن صاحب القوة الحدسية يعلم أن هناك واحدة من العلل وإن لم يتعين عندنا ولم يمكن للعقل أن يشير إليها إشارة على التعيين وأن تلك الواحدة مع المعلول الأخير محيطة بما
And he who adduced it admitted—calling it the 'Throne proof' (burhān ʿarshī), and he is the author of al-Ishrāq (Suhrawardī)—that it is intuitive (ḥadsī), needing intuition to know its correctness. This is because if the causes were finite, it would appear completely that everything except one specific cause lies between it and the last effect. But if they are assumed infinite, as in our case, this meaning does not appear in it, since there is not conceived a single cause except that there is another cause before it. So how can the confinement be conceived? However, the possessor of intuitive power (al-quwwa al-ḥadsīyya) knows that there is a certain cause, even if it is not determined for us and the mind cannot point to it specifically, and that that one together with the last effect encompasses what is between them.
Source pages p. 181

Commentary
This passage is an acknowledgment by Suhrawardī (the Illuminationist philosopher) that the bounding argument just presented is not a purely demonstrative proof but an intuitive (ḥadsī) one. The reason is that if the series of causes were finite, it would be obvious that there is a cause that bounds the series from one side. But if the series is infinite, there is no such obvious bounding cause—every cause has a cause before it. The mind cannot directly identify the bounding term. Nevertheless, the person with intuitive power (al-quwwa al-ḥadsīyya) can grasp that there must be some cause that, together with the last effect, encompasses everything between them. This intuitive knowledge, though not fully determinate, is sufficient to establish the finitude of the series. The term 'Throne proof' (burhān ʿarshī) is used by Suhrawardī for such intuitive arguments.

Key Terms
حدس
برهان عرشي
صاحب الإشراق
قوة حدسية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The bounding proof is purely demonstrative and does not require any special faculty.
Correction: Suhrawardī admits it is intuitive and requires intuitive power (al-quwwa al-ḥadsīyya) to know its correctness.

Checkpoint
Why does Suhrawardī say the bounding proof is intuitive (ḥadsī)?
A) Because it requires empirical observation.
B) Because in an infinite series, the bounding cause is not evident to ordinary reasoning.
C) Because the proof is based on scripture.
D) Because the proof is invalid.

Key Takeaway
The bounding proof of the finitude of causes relies on intuitive insight, not pure demonstration, because in an infinite series the bounding term is not evident to ordinary reason.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

The Fourth Proof: Inequality of Effects and Causes
Presents the fourth proof that infinite regress causes inequality in the number of effects and causes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the fourth proof against infinite regress based on the inequality of effects to causes and why it only applies to one-sided regress.

Core Idea
Infinite regress would break the perfect pairing of cause and effect.

The fourth proof examines the relation between causes and effects in an infinite chain. If the regress is one-sided, the number of effect-relations must exceed cause-relations, which contradicts their necessary equivalence. This lesson unpacks the argument and its limitation.

Guided Path
1
Understand the conditional statement
Read the first part of the passage which states the conditional: if infinite regress occurs, then effects outnumber causes. Notice how the reasoning is built.
The proof assumes a chain starting from a final effect and going backward.
2
Grasp the exception (correlation argument)
The passage then argues that the consequent (inequality) is false because causality and effectness are genuine correlatives that must be equal in number.
This uses the principle of taḍāyuf ḥaqīqī.
3
Note the scope limitation
The commentary explicitly states that this proof does not apply when the regression is infinite on both sides (i.e., no first cause).
Previous proofs did not have this limitation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الْوَجْهُ (الرَّابِعُ: لَوْ تَسَلْسَلَ الْعِلَلُ إِلَى غَيْرِ النِّهَايَةِ لَزِمَ زِيَادَةُ عَدَدِ الْمَعْلُولِ عَلَى عَدَدِ الْعِلَلِ، أَيْ لَزَادَ عَدَدُ الْمَعْلُولِيَّةِ عَلَى عَدَدِ الْعِلِّيَّةِ ) وَالتَّالِي بَاطِلٌ. أَمَّا الشَّرْطِيَّةُ فَلَأَنَّا إِذَا فَرَضْنَا سِلْسِلَةً مِنْ مَعْلُولٍ أَخِيرٍ إِلَى غَيْرِ النِّهَايَةِ، كَانَ كُلُّ مَا هُوَ عِلَّةٌ فِيهَا أَيْ فِي تِلْكَ السِّلْسِلَةِ، فَهُوَ مَعْلُولٌ، لِأَنَّ كُلَّ وَاحِدٍ مِمَّا عَدَا الْمَعْلُولِ الْأَخِيرِ فِيهَا يَكُونُ عِلَّةً لِمَا بَعْدَهُ، وَمَعْلُولاً لِمَا قَبْلَهُ مِنْ غَيْرِ عَكْسٍ. فَإِنَّ الْأَخِيرَ مَعْلُولٌ وَلَيْسَ بِعِلَّةٍ لِشَيْءٍ مِنْ تِلْكَ السِّلْسِلَةِ، فَقَدْ زَادَ عَدَدُ الْمَعْلُولِيَّةِ عَلَى عَدَدِ الْعِلِّيَّةِ. وَلَوْ كَانَتِ الْعِلَلُ مُتَنَاهِيَةً لَمْ يَلْزَمْ ذَلِكَ، فَإِنَّ مَبْدَأَ السِّلْسِلَةِ عِلَّةٌ وَلَيْسَ بِمَعْلُولٍ وَمُنْتَهَاهَا أَعْنِي الْمَعْلُولَ الْأَخِيرَ مَعْلُولٌ وَلَيْسَ بِعِلَّةٍ فَيَتَسَاوَى عَدَدُ الْعِلِّيَّةِ وَالْمَعْلُولِيَّةِ. ( وَأَمَّا الِاسْتِثْنَائِيَّةُ ) وَهِيَ بُطْلَانُ التَّالِي فَلِأَنَّ) الْعِلَّةَ وَالْمَعْلُولَ أَيِ الْعِلِّيَّةَ (وَالْمَعْلُولِيَّةَ (مُتَضَايِفَانِ) تَضَايُفاً حَقِيقِيًّا ( وَمِنْ لَوَازِمِهِمَا التَّكَافُؤُ فِي الْوُجُودِ ) أَيْ إِذَا وُجِدَ أَحَدُ الْمُتَضَايِفَيْنِ الْحَقِيقِيَّيْنِ وُجِدَ الْآخَرُ قَطْعاً، فَلَا بُدَّ أَنْ يُوجَدَ بِإِزَاءِ كُلِّ وَاحِدٍ ) مِنْ أَحَدِهِمَا ( وَاحِدٌ مِنَ الْآخَرِ، فَيَكُونَانِ مُتَسَاوِيَيْنِ فِي الْعَدَدِ ضَرُورَةً). قَوْلُهُ الرَّابِعُ) لَوْ تَسَلْسَلَ (الْعِلَلُ هَذَا الدَّلِيلُ لَا يَجْرِي فِيمَا إِذَا كَانَ عَدَمُ التَّنَاهِي مِنَ الْجَانِبَيْنِ أَيِ الْعِلَّةِ وَالْمَعْلُولِ بِخِلَافِ الْأَدِلَّةِ السَّابِقَةِ.
The fourth aspect: if causes were to regress infinitely, it would necessitate an increase in the number of effects over the number of causes, i.e., the number of effect-relations would exceed the number of cause-relations. And the consequent is false. As for the conditional: because if we assume a chain from a final effect to infinity, every thing that is a cause in it, i.e., in that chain, is an effect, because every one except the final effect in it is a cause for what is after it and an effect for what is before it without the converse. For the final one is an effect and not a cause for anything of that chain, so the number of effect-relations exceeds the number of cause-relations. And if the causes were finite, that would not follow, for the beginning of the chain is a cause and not an effect, and its end, i.e., the final effect, is an effect and not a cause, so the numbers of cause-relations and effect-relations are equal. (As for the exception) which is the falsity of the consequent: because cause and effect, i.e., causality (ʿilliyya) and effectness (maʿlūliyya), are two correlatives (mutadāyifān) in a genuine correlation (taḍāyuf ḥaqīqī), and among their necessary concomitants is equivalence in existence, i.e., if one of the two genuine correlatives exists, the other exists necessarily. So there must exist in exchange for each one of them one from the other, so they are necessarily equal in number. His statement (the fourth): 'if causes were to regress' – this proof does not apply when the infinity is from both sides, i.e., the cause and effect, unlike the previous proofs.
Source pages p. 182

Commentary
This passage presents and explains the fourth proof against infinite regress. It begins by stating the proof: if there were an infinite regress of causes in one direction (from a final effect upward), then the number of effect-relations would exceed the number of cause-relations. The reasoning is that in such a chain, every cause except the first is also an effect of a prior cause, while the final effect is only an effect and not a cause. Thus, the count of effect-relations (one per item except possibly the first) is greater than the count of cause-relations (one per item except the last). If the chain were finite, the first cause would have no cause, and the last effect no effect, making the numbers equal. The falsity of the consequent is then argued through the concept of genuine correlation (taḍāyuf ḥaqīqī) between causality and effectness: they must be exactly paired, so their numbers cannot differ. The commentator notes that this proof only works when the regress is one-sided (from the effect side); if both sides are infinite, the argument fails because every term is both cause and effect, so the counts remain equal.

Key Terms
العلة
المعلول
العلية
المعلولية
المتضايفان
التضايف الحقيقي
التكافؤ في الوجود

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think this proof applies to any infinite regress, even when both cause and effect sides are infinite.
Correction: The passage explicitly states the proof only applies when the regress is one-sided (from the effect side). If both sides are infinite, each term is both cause and effect, so the numbers remain equal.

Checkpoint
Why does the fourth proof fail when the regression is from both sides?
A) Because causes and effects are not truly correlative.
B) Because every term is both cause and effect, so the counts remain equal.
C) Because the proof requires actual infinite existence.
D) Because the proof relies on a false assumption.

Key Takeaway
The fourth proof shows that one-sided infinite regress would disrupt the necessary equality between causes and effects, but it does not apply when both sides are infinite.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the universe requires a first cause because an infinite regress would break the necessary pairing of cause and effect, then what does that say about the ultimate purpose your own life is part of? Are you living as if your existence is linked to a First Cause, or do you act as if the chain of meaning stops with you?
?
The proof shows that the number of causes and effects must be equal—there is no room for imbalance. In your own spiritual life, are there areas where you accept 'imbalance'—too much concern for effects (worldly results) and not enough for causes (your intentions and actions)? Will you commit to restoring the balance by focusing on the cause of your deeds?
?
If genuine correlatives like cause and effect necessarily come in pairs, then your actions (causes) and their consequences (effects) are inseparably linked. Are you taking full responsibility for the effects you cause, or do you try to disconnect them? What would it mean for you to acknowledge that every cause you set in motion will have an effect that you cannot escape?

Applying the Correlation Proof to Infinite Regress
al-Iji applies the correlation argument to one-sided infinite regress.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the correlation argument demonstrates the impossibility of infinite regress in a chain of causes and effects by showing inequality in the number of relations.

Core Idea
The correlation proof shows that infinite regress breaks the necessary equality of cause and effect relations.

In this passage, al-Iji explains that the correlation argument can be applied to a chain of causes and effects. If the chain were infinite, the number of cause-relations would exceed effect-relations because the first cause is not an effect. This contradiction proves that infinite regress is impossible.

Guided Path
1
Read the argument carefully
Read the passage once, noting the claim that in infinite regress, cause-relations are more numerous than effect-relations.
Pay attention to the logical structure: assumption, deduction, contrast with finite.
2
Compare with the finite case
Notice that if the chain is finite, the numbers are equal. This highlights the problem with infinity.
The equality in finite case is presented as the natural order.
3
Apply to philosophers' events
Understand how the argument applies to the infinite series of past events posited by philosophers. The key is the violation of equivalence between priority and posteriority.

Source Text

وَهَذَا الْوَجْهُ جَارٍ فِي تَسَلْسُلِ الْمُتَضَايِفَاتِ فَيُقَالُ: لَوْ تَسَلْسَلَتِ الْمَعْلُولَاتُ إِلَى غَيْرِ النِّهَايَةِ لَزَادَ عَدَدُ الْعِلِّيَّةِ عَلَى عَدَدِ الْمَعْلُولِيَّةِ؛ لِأَنَّ كُلَّ مَا هُوَ مَعْلُولٌ فِي هَذِهِ السِّلْسِلَةِ، فَهُوَ عِلَّةٌ مِنْ غَيْرِ عَكْسٍ فَإِنَّ الْعِلَّةَ الْأُولَى لَيْسَتْ مَعْلُولَةً مَعَ كَوْنِهَا عِلَّةً، وَلَوْ كَانَتِ الْمَعْلُولَاتُ مُتَنَاهِيَةً لَكَانَ الْمَعْلُولُ الْأَخِيرُ مَعْلُولاً، وَلَمْ يَكُنْ عِلَّةً، فَيَتَسَاوَى عَدَدُ الْعِلِّيَّةِ وَالْمَعْلُولِيَّةِ كَمَا هُوَ حَقُّهُمَا. وَبِالْجُمْلَةِ فَإِنَّ التَّسَلْسُلَ فِي الْمُتَضَايِفَاتِ يَسْتَلْزِمُ كَوْنَ إِحْدَى الْإِضَافَتَيْنِ أَزْيَدَ عَدَداً مِنَ الْأُخْرَى، وَهُوَ بَاطِلٌ. قَوْلُهُ: ( وَهَذَا الْوَجْهُ جَارٍ فِي تَسَلْسُلِ الْمُتَضَايِفَاتِ إِلَخ) عَلِيَّاتٍ كَانَتْ أَوْ مَعْلُولِيَّاتٍ مُجْتَمِعَةً أَوْ مُتَعَاقِبَةً، فَيَجْرِي فِي الْحَوَادِثِ الْغَيْرِ الْمُتَنَاهِيَةِ الَّتِي أَثْبَتَهَا الْفَلَاسِفَةُ فِي رَبْطِ الْحَادِثِ بِالْقَدِيمِ لِاتِّصَافِ آحَادِهَا بِالسَّابِقِيَّةِ وَالْمَسْبُوقِيَّةِ مَعَ تَنَاهِيهَا فِي جَانِبِ الِاسْتِقْبَالِ، فَلَوْ تَسَلْسَلَتْ إِلَى غَيْرِ النِّهَايَةِ فِي جَانِبِ الْمَاضِي لَزِمَ زِيَادَةُ عَدَدِ الْمَسْبُوقِيَّاتِ عَلَى عَدَدِ السَّابِقِيَّاتِ وَهُوَ يَسْتَلْزِمُ بُطْلَانَ التَّكَافُؤِ بَيْنَهُمَا. وَمِنْ هَذَا ظَهَرَ أَنَّ هَذَا الْبُرْهَانَ لَا يَجْرِي فِي التَّسَلْسُلِ مِنَ الْجَانِبَيْنِ، لِأَنَّ كُلَّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْ آحَادِ تِلْكَ السِّلْسِلَةِ مَوْصُوفٌ بِالْعِلِّيَّةِ وَالْمَعْلُولِيَّةِ فَلَا زِيَادَةَ لِعَدَدِ أَحَدِ الْمُتَضَايِفَيْنِ عَلَى الْآخَرِ. وَمَا قَالَهُ بَعْضُ النَّاظِرِينَ نَاقِلاً عَنِ الْمُحَقِّقِ الدَّوَانِيِّ فِي جَرَيَانِهِ فِيهِ مِنْ أَنَّا إِذَا أَخَذْنَا مِنْ تِلْكَ السِّلْسِلَةِ سِلْسِلَةً غَيْرَ مُتَنَاهِيَةٍ مِنْ مَعْلُولٍ مُعَيَّنٍ وَتَصَاعَدْنَا فِي الْعِلَلِ الْغَيْرِ الْمُتَنَاهِيَةِ فَلَا بُدَّ أَنْ يَكُونَ عَدَدُ الْعِلِّيَّاتِ وَالْمَعْلُولِيَّاتِ الْوَاقِعَةِ فِي تِلْكَ الْقِطْعَةِ مُتَكَافِئَةً، ضَرُورَةَ أَنَّ الْعِلِّيَّةَ الَّتِي تُضَايِفُ الْمَعْلُولَاتِ الْوَاقِعَةَ فِيهَا لَا يُمْكِنُ أَنْ يَكُونَ فِيمَا تَحْتَ تِلْكَ الْمَعْلُولِيَّاتِ، وَهُوَ ظَاهِرٌ. فَفِيهِ بَحْثٌ لِأَنَّ كُلَّ مَعْلُولِيَّةٍ فِي تِلْكَ الْقِطْعَةِ مُضَايِفَةٌ لِلْعِلِّيَةِ الَّتِي قَبْلَهُ فَالْمَعْلُولِيَّةُ الَّتِي فِي الْمَعْلُولِ الْمُعَيَّنِ الَّذِي أُخِذَ مَبْدَأً مُضَايِفَةٌ لِلْعِلِّيَةِ الَّتِي قَبْلَهُ بِلَا وَاسِطَةٍ وَهَلُمَّ جَراً. وَلَيْسَ شَيْءٌ مِنَ السِّلْسِلَةِ غَيْرَ مَوْصُوفٍ بِالْعِلِّيَةِ فَلَا زِيَادَةَ لِعَدَدِ الْمَعْلُولِيَّاتِ عَلَى عَدَدِ الْعِلِّيَّاتِ حَتَّى يُسْتَدَلَّ بِهَا عَلَى بُطْلَانِ التَّكَافُؤِ الْمُسْتَلْزِمِ لِبُطْلَانِ التَّضَايُفِ، بِخِلَافِ مَا إِذَا كَانَتِ السِّلْسِلَةُ مُتَنَاهِيَةً فِي الْجَانِبَيْنِ، فَإِنَّهُ يَتَّصِفُ الْمَبْدَأُ بِالْمَعْلُولِيَّةِ فَقَطْ أَوِ الْعِلِّيَةِ وَسَائِرُ الْآحَادِ مَوْصُوفَةٌ بِهِمَا فَيَزِيدُ عَدَدُ آحَادِ أَحَدِ الْجَانِبَيْنِ.
And this aspect applies to the regress of correlatives, so it is said: if effects were to regress infinitely, the number of cause-relations would exceed the number of effect-relations, because everything that is an effect in this chain is a cause without the converse, for the first cause is not an effect while being a cause. And if the effects were finite, the final effect would be an effect and not a cause, so the numbers of cause- and effect-relations would be equal as is their right. In short, regress in correlatives necessitates that one of the two relations be greater in number than the other, which is false. His statement: ('And this aspect applies to the regress of correlatives etc.') – whether they are causal relations or effect relations, simultaneous or successive. So it applies to the infinite events that the philosophers posited in linking the temporal to the eternal, due to the description of their individuals with priority and posteriority, while being finite on the future side. So if they were to regress infinitely on the past side, the number of posteriorities would exceed the number of priorities, which entails the nullification of equivalence between them. And from this it appears that this proof does not apply to regress from both sides, because every individual of that chain is described with causehood and effecthood, so there is no increase in the number of one correlative over the other. And what some thinkers said, quoting from al-Muḥaqqiq al-Dawānī, about its application to it – that if we take from that chain an infinite chain from a specific effect and ascend through the infinite causes, then the numbers of cause-relations and effect-relations occurring in that segment must be equal, necessarily, because the causehood that correlates with the effecthoods occurring in it cannot be among those effecthoods, which is apparent – there is discussion about it, because every effecthood in that segment is correlative to the causehood that precedes it, so the effecthood in the specific effect taken as a beginning is correlative to the causehood before it directly, and so on. And nothing in the chain is undescribed with causehood, so there is no increase in the number of effecthoods over causehoods that could be used to prove the falsity of equivalence entailing the falsity of correlation, unlike when the chain is finite on both sides, for then the beginning is described with effecthood only or causehood and the rest are described with both, so the number of individuals of one side increases.
Source pages p. 183

Commentary
This passage extends the previous argument to correlatives (al-mutadāyifāt). It first restates the point: in an infinite regress of effects, the number of cause-relations would exceed effect-relations because the first cause is not an effect. If finite, the numbers equal. The commentator then notes that this argument applies to both causal and effect relations whether simultaneous or temporal, and gives the example of an infinite series of events on the past side (as philosophers argue for linking events to the eternal). If regress were infinite in the past, the number of posteriorities (masbūqiyyāt) would exceed priorities (sābiqiyyāt), violating the necessary equivalence of correlatives. Then the commentator clarifies that this proof does not work when the regress is from both sides (e.g., infinite in both past and future, or both cause and effect sides), because each term is both cause and effect, so the numbers remain equal. The passage ends with a refutation of al-Dawānī's claim that the proof can be applied even when both sides are infinite by isolating a segment. The commentator argues that in that segment, every effecthood is precisely matched to a preceding causehood, so no inequality arises. The proof only works when the chain has a definite beginning (one-sided).
